***Standing: \--*** These two illustrious souls, setting aside their high moral and spiritual station, which manifested itself in kindness and compassion towards all people, evinced the utmost liberality in assisting the weak and the destitute, and were moreover extolled and celebrated for these exalted attributes. In respect of their commercial standing too, they enjoyed no inconsiderable reputation. It was customary during that period, when the postal service had been but newly founded, for those making postal deliveries to take the commercial letters and communications to the caravanserais and commercial houses, and, calling out the names of their recipients, invite them to receive their missives. According to the accounts of eye-witnesses, when the postal functionary arrived at the Gulshan caravanserai, and called out the names of the recipients of the letters, more than eighty percent of the incoming items were announced to be for Áqá Mírzá Hasan and Áqá Mírzá Husayn. This circumstance, it may fairly be stated, was a matter of great astonishment, as well as of envy, to the other tradespeople.

***Wealth: \--*** The wealth of the aforesaid honoured brothers was the talk of both high and low. It is known for example that no sooner had they been arrested and confined in the residence of the Imám-Jum'ih, and afterwards in that of Zillu's-Sultán, than their distant and near relatives transported from their homes to other places huge quantities and stores of coin, gold and jewels, which remained to the last days in the families of the heirs. Even so, after the martyrdom a considerable quantity of gold was carried off as spoil and plunder by the government officials of the time. The large sum they sought of the She-Serpent, so engendering the enmity that resulted in their martyrdom, constitutes moreover a clear proof of the superabundance of their wealth. It is known that on the very day of their martyrdom there arrived in Isfahán a caravan laden with their wares, which, after it had proceeded to the Maydán-i-Naqsh-i-Jihán, known as the Maydán-i-Sháh, and its ownership been ascertained, was confiscated in its entirety by the government.

***Generosity: \--*** It is known that the assistance of the two brothers was extended without distinction to all people, including even Ramadán the executioner, who was afterwards compelled to put them to death. For a while Ramadán sought by various pretexts to put off the deed, considering himself to be indebted to the two brothers for various favours they had rendered him.

*One or two instances of the results of the martyrdom: \--*

***1 --*** Banánu'l-Mulk, the father of Fadlu'lláh-i-Banán-i-Shírází, who was one of the well-known agents of Zillu's-Sultán, told the late Mír-Panj Ja'far-Qulí Khán, the Mu'azzamu'l-Mulk, who was among the respected Kháns of Firaydan, and a high-ranking officer of the old Afváj, of an interview conducted by Zillu's-Sultán in the Chihil-Sutún Pavilion preliminary to these actions. Having summoned the Twin Shining Lights before him, Zillu's-Sultán, with perfect solicitude and kindness, proceeded to admonish and advise them in the following terms: "I do not wish to have you, who are the children of the Prophet, put to death. Merely to silence the Imám-Jum'ih and Shaykh Báqir, do ye declare only 'We are not Bahá'ís.' I will myself then dissuade them from seeking your death; restore all your affairs and assets; and see to it that the utmost love and kindness is observed towards you." With the utmost firmness and steadfastness the two brothers made reply, "To do so would be for us impossible and impermissible." The more the prince insisted, the more the brothers persisted in their refusal. At last he grew angry, and, with all the force he could muster, struck with a boot the head, the face and the mouth of the two brothers, and gave orders for their execution.

So profound an impression did the relation of this occurrence make upon the late Mu'azzamu'l-Mulk that he was guided to embrace the Truth. As a result, a large family accepted the Blessed Cause, forming the nucleus of the believers in Firaydan.

*Photograph of the illumined resting-place of the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs*

***2 --*** Áqá Mírzá Ja'far-i-Thábit, who for years pursued in Isfahán the trade of a haberdasher, and afterwards, as a result of the upheaval and tumult, migrated to Tihrán, related the following: "On the day of the martyrdom I, being unaware of what had taken place, happened to pass through the Maydán-i-Sháh. A great multitude had lined its sides, while soldiers had occupied its central space. Upon my asking what was afoot, I was told, 'They have killed two Siyyids who had become Bábís. Their bodies even now lie fallen in the centre of the square.' This announcement that they had killed two Siyyids who were Bábís caused me, despite myself, to become fearfully agitated. I wanted to cry out 'Why have they slain the children of the Prophet!' A person who was standing nearby however took me by the hand, and, with gentle counsels, restrained me from this course. Leading me away from the square, he began to talk with me, explaining what the term 'Bábí' truly signified. In short, having made clear to me the reality of the matter, he was the cause of my becoming a believer."

Of the countless similar occurrences, whereby many souls have been guided to the Truth, the above two instances have remained in my mind.

***Fatal illness of the Imám-Jum'ih: \--*** As is well known throughout the city, a boil appeared on the neck of the Imám-Jum'ih from whose putrid odour all his family members shrank in disgust and loathing. They transported him to the Garden of Shams-Ábád, where he returned to his native abode. It was known that Shaykh Báqir hesitated a little on account of their holy lineage before issuing the death sentence; but the Imám-Jum'ih, who was its principal cause and instigator, clapped his hand upon his neck, exclaiming, "Upon my neck be it (indicating that he would answer for it with his life): the blood of these twain may legitimately be shed."

*Photograph showing several views of the entrance door and the interior of the home of the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs*

***Áqá Mírzá Ismá'íl: \--*** The other brother of the two martyrs, who resorted to taqíyyih, was the son-in-law of the late Áqá Muhammad-Taqí, son of the late Hájj Mullá Shafí'-i-Khú'í. Belonging as they did to the class of the 'ulamá', when they learned of the two brothers' acceptance of the Blessed Cause they took preventive action to acquit Áqá Mírzá Ismá'íl of any such imputation, and obtained from Shaykh Báqir a ruling in this regard, which was reproduced verbatim in the preceding pages.

***The recent litigation: \--*** At the time when the modern judiciary was set up by the late Dávar, the heirs of the late Áqá Mírzá Ismá'íl, in order to recover the property held in pledge by the Imám-Jum'ih, and which was in the name of the brothers, brought a suit before the courts of law; but because of the indifference of the legal representatives of the heirs on the one hand, and the excessive influence of the previous possessors of the property on the other, they were content to end the proceedings on the basis of a vain and empty compromise; naught was gained; and the file was recorded as without effect. Before these proceedings too, during the period of despotic rule, the heirs had, at the time of Zillu's-Sultán, brought a case before the Sharí'ah courts and government departments; but the usurpers, apart from having actual possession of the property, stifled the proceedings by paying an exorbitant bribe to Zillu's-Sultán. Since one of the heirs, the late Khánum Siyyid, daughter of Áqá Mírzá Ismá'íl, was the wife of Zillu's-Sultán, the prince in truth stood himself indirectly to benefit from the case; but having already obtained his share in the form of a bribe, he chose to overlook the matter. On the day when he ordered the proceedings closed, he threw down before his wife Khánum Siyyid a three-túmán note, saying: "Siyyid Jún, here is a share for thee too."

*Photographs showing (above) the reception room of the house, and (below) the place of confinement of, the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs in Isfahán*

In a blessed talk concerning the martyrdom of the Twin Shining Lights delivered in Haifa in 1332 A.H. His Holiness 'Abdu'l-Bahá -- exalted be His praise -- has said.

*His most sweet utterance:*

Zillu's-Sultán told me in Paris, "I wish to explain to thee a certain matter. Prithee give ear unto this account." I replied, "Say on! What harm is there?" He said, "I wish to describe for thee the circumstances of the case of the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs." Taking then an oath, he asserted: "This deed was my father's doing. This sin did not originate from me. This transgression is upon my father's head. He wrote to me, 'Bring to thee the brothers and slay them.' I wrote, 'The brothers (that is, the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs) are no ordinary people, that I should bring them hither and slay them. They are eminent and respected citizens of this town. If these be put to death, the people of Isfahán will be greatly perturbed and alarmed. It is not in the interests of the state to slay them.' Again the answer came, 'Questionless thou must slay them.' I wrote, 'This is a very difficult matter. Shouldst thou command it, let me bring them hither and induce them to recant. These are Siyyids, descendants of the Prophet, of unbroken lineage.' A third order arrived: 'Without further recourse, do thou immediately upon receipt of this order bring them to thee and slay them.' First, I sent to them various people with instructions to advise them on my behalf: 'The matter standeth thus. I am acting under duress, and, except ye recant, I have no choice. I will gather the 'ulamá, and bring you before them in a meeting: there do ye announce your recantation. By this means shall I be able to save you from this predicament.' But they would not have it. I was forced to bring them into the government prison. There too I privily sent to them numerous people in order to admonish them, and convey to them on my behalf, 'This is the royal command: it cannot be disregarded. Come now, and announce your recantation: forgo this matter, for otherwise Sháh Bábá will never acquiesce.' Yet still they would not accept. Finally, I myself summoned them at night, and said, 'Áqá Siyyid Husayn, Áqá Siyyid Hasan. This matter hath assumed extremely grave proportions. Sháh Bábá is inflexibly resolved upon your death. There remaineth no expedient at my disposal but to tell the Sháh that ye have recanted. Otherwise, if I do not put you to death, Sháh Bábá will hold me responsible. I do not say that ye should speak evil. Say only, "We are not Bahá'ís," and I will take care of the rest.' They said, 'It is not possible. We are Bahá'ís. Yá Bahá'u'l-Abhá!' However oft I repeated, 'Áqá Mírzá Husayn, Áqá Mírzá Hasan. They will *kill* you!,' they would not hear me. They said, 'Yá Bahá'u'l-Abhá!' I did whatever was needful. They utterly refused to accept. The Sháh for his part insisted with the utmost importunity that they should die. I could see that if I did not put them to death, Sháh Bábá would kill me." Such is the story Zillu's-Sultán related to me. He said, "However oft I told them, 'Say only "We are not Bahá'ís,"' they would not have it, but rather repeated, 'Yá Bahá'u'l-Abhá! Yá Bahá'u'l-Abhá!'" *Finis*.

As will have been noted, the two most pure corses of the Twin Shining Lights Al-Hasan and Al-Husayn -- may the peace of God be upon them -- were interred in the Takhtih-Fúlád cemetery. After a while Áqá Mírzá Muhammad-Sádiq, the son of his honour the Beloved of Martyrs, submitted a petition to the Sacred Court of His Holiness 'Abdu'l-Bahá -- exalted be His praise -- requesting leave, should His blessed permission be vouchsafed to this effect, to translate the most pure corses of the twin beatific martyrs from the Takhtih-Fúlád cemetery of Isfahán to the house of the martyrs, which was their place of residence. A Blessed Tablet was revealed in reply, importing that such a measure was not then advisable, and should accordingly be deferred to some future date. The actual wording of this Tablet is as follows.

*His most sweet utterance:*

* He *

*Isfahán. The distinguished scion of him who attained unto the Abhá Kingdom, the Beloved of Martyrs, upon him be the Glory of God, the Most Glorious*

He is God

O thou true servant of the Abhá Beauty! Although some time hath passed ere our last exchange of correspondence, yet thine illumined conscience is aware, and doth bear me witness, that no moment have I rested without thinking of thee; and ever have I turned my face unto the Threshold of Oneness, tearfully imploring that thou mightest be under all circumstances a model of servitude unto the Essence of Oneness, and occupied with whatsoever is graceful, lasting and becoming. Praise be to God that thou art assisted and confirmed, and the object of the glances of His loving-kindness.

Thou didst write concerning the translation of the two holy and pure temples from their present location to the frequented fane. Having regard to the need for wisdom, such a measure is not at present permissible, for the people of enmity and rancour lie in ambush, whilst the malevolent lurk in hidden corners. Upon the slightest pretext they would arise to desecrate the sepulchre. Yet in future -- that is, erelong -- it will fall out happily. 'Ayn 'Ayn

In 1322 A.H.S. the Spiritual Assembly of Isfahán, acting upon the instructions of his Holiness the Guardian of the Cause of God -- exalted be his praise -- as conveyed by the Sacred National Assembly of the Bahá'ís of Írán, transferred the sanctified mortal remains of the Twin Shining Lights from Takhtih-Fúlád to a place in the vicinity of the grave of the eloquent and renowned teacher of the Cause of God, Mrs. Keith Ransom-Kehler. This wondrous spot, situated beside the Záyandih Rúd in a beautiful surrounding filled with trees, verdure and flowers, is today a holy site of visitation for the Friends of God. The grave of the famed teacher lies at but a little distance from the luminous resting-place of the Twin Shining Lights; and only recently the Spiritual Assembly of Isfahán has, at the instance of his Holiness the Guardian of the Cause of God, taken the step of transferring also, from the Takhtih-Fúlád cemetery to a place near the tombs of Mrs. Ransom-Kehler and the Twin Shining Lights, the mortal remains of the detached teacher of the Cause of God, Áqá Mírzá Mihdí Ikhvánu's-Safáy-i-Yazdí.

Since the subject has arisen, we shall at this point interpose a few words concerning that famous teacher and paragon of eloquence -- and now possessor of the glorious station of martyrdom -- Mrs. Ransom-Kehler:

The subject (of whose life, for the sake of brevity, no account will here be given), arrived in Írán at the behest of the Guardian, and after she had spent some time in Tihrán and elsewhere meeting with the friends, it was decided that she would journey to Isfahán, and afterwards proceed to Shíráz. The National Assembly accordingly advised the Spiritual Assembly of Isfahán of her impending visit; and on the afternoon of Friday 14 Mihr 1311 A.H.S. she arrived in that city. A fitting reception was held for her by the Spiritual Assembly, to describe all of whose extremely diverse proceedings would be beyond the purview of this notebook. Whilst in Isfahán Mrs. Kehler took ill with the smallpox, and eventually, after having been confined to her sickbed for two weeks, she ascended to the Abhá Kingdom on 2 Ábán 1312 A.H.S. (9 'Ilm 90 B.E. of the Bahá'í calendar, corresponding to 24 October 1933, or 5 Rajab 1352 A.H.) Her body was at first deposited in the Eternal Rose Garden, which was situated in Takhtih-Fúlád; then after a while, when the present location had been made ready, she was translated thither. After her passing a telegram arrived from the Guardian, in which he conferred upon her the rank of martyrdom, including her in the company of the Hands of the Cause of God. Upon her be the forgiveness of God and His Glory.

* * *

*Visitation Tablet of the Martyrs*

The honoured Maidservant of God, Rúhá Khánum-i-Mahbúbíy-i-Maghzí wrote to the court of his Holiness the Guardian of the Cause of God -- exalted be his sovereignty -- beseeching that a Tablet of Visitation might issue from his blessed pen in honour of the martyrs of Isfahán.

The following blessed directive was issued in response to her petition.

*Isfahán. The Maidservant of God Rúhá Khánum-i-Mahbúbí, upon her be the Glory of God, the Most Glorious*

The petition presented by that maidservant of the Sacred Divine Threshold, dated 16 / 3 / 1312, arrived at the sacred court of our gracious and loving liege, his Holiness the Guardian of the Cause of God -- may our souls be a sacrifice for his favours -- and its contents, indicative alike of felicity and spirituality, brought gladness and satisfaction to his blessed being. Thou didst mention the martyrs of the Land of Sád, beseeching that a Tablet of Visitation might issue from his blessed pen. He said: "Write thou: 'Whatsoever hath emanated from the Pen of the Most High, and of the Centre of the Covenant, concerning the martyrs of that land is an inestimable treasure, which the treasuries of heaven and earth can never rival. They are a sufficient bounty and a plenteous bestowal. It is not permissible for a Tablet of Visitation to proceed from the pen of this servant.'" He added: "At times of supplication and devotion in the Holy Shrines, this servant of the Sacred Threshold, with perfect humility and lowliness, beseecheth that the degrees of those sanctified souls may be exalted; while for the survivors of the martyrs I seek from the Threshold of His Holiness, the Lord of mankind, assistance, confirmation, and everlasting happiness." The sheet of delightful verses came too under the gracious and benevolent notice of his most holy being. Again he expressed his kind and loving sentiments towards that attracted and consecrated leaf. Written by his blessed order. Núri'd-Dín Zayn, 15 Núr 90, 19 June 1933

(Written in the Guardian's own hand) "*... May God make thee a sign of bestowal, a standard of victory, and a lamp of guidance among the believing maidservants and the well-assured leaves in that distant clime. The servant of His Threshold, Shoghi*"

*Visitation Tablet in Honour of the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs*

*Set then thyself towards the Holy Martyrs' Tombs and the Exalted Shrines,* *and, when thou hast known, hast found, and come before them, stand and say:*

The first light that shone forth from the horizon of the revelation of the Face of your Lord, the Creator of the Heavens, be upon you, O ye the manifestations of fidelity, and the dawning-places of names in the kingdom of creation! I testify that through you the standards of victory have been manifested, the ensigns of guidance have been hoisted, the horizon of steadfastness hath been illumined, and the breeze of God hath been wafted amidst mankind; and through you the glory of sacrifice hath been renewed, and that which hath caused the hearts and minds to marvel hath appeared. It is ye who sacrificed all that ye possessed, your spirits, your every limb and vein, in the path of God, your Well-Beloved and your hearts' Desire. It is ye whom neither the wrong of the oppressor, nor the blame of the blamer, nor the onslaught of every disbeliever who turned away from God when he came invested with a sovereignty that hath encompassed all who are in heaven and on earth, could deter from following in His way. I testify that the Celestial Concourse, and with them the dwellers of the All-Glorious Tabernacle, have bewailed your agony; while on behalf of every believer the Tongue of God, the Help in Peril, the Self-Subsisting, hath spoken: "Verily, we are God's, and unto Him shall we return." In all conditions, praise be to God, the Lord of all that was and shall be.

*Then beseech of God whatsoever thou desirest of His bounty; He, verily, is the All-Glorious, the All-Loving:*

Upon thee be an effulgence of supernal Glory, O thou dayspring of fidelity, from God, the Creator of the Heavens. I testify that through thee the City of Servitude hath been adorned; its standards have been hoisted; its gates have been decked forth; and its songsters have warbled. I testify that thou didst set thy face towards God, and didst speak forth His praise amidst His servants. Blessed art thou, and thy brother, he on whose account the denizens of the Most Sublime Paradise wept sore; and blessed are all who direct themselves towards you; who inhale your fragrance; who follow in your footsteps; and who choose the part of charity towards your kinsfolk now that ye are gone.

*Direct then thy gaze towards Kázim, who won the crown of Supreme Sacrifice in the path of God, the Lord of Mankind, and say:*

Upon thee be the Glory of God, O thou who didst sacrifice thy whole being in the way of God, the Lord of the worlds. The first fragrance that was diffused from the raiment of the mercy of thy Lord, the Possessor of all names, rest upon thee, O thou star shining above the horizon of fidelity, thou who didst ever fix thy gaze upon the Supreme Horizon. I testify that thou didst set thyself towards Him on a Day when every disbeliever had repudiated Him; didst lay hold upon the Book when every infidel had discarded it; didst acknowledge that which the Tongue of Grandeur spake when every gainsayer had denied it; and didst quaff the choice wine of mystic meanings when every hypocrite had forsaken it. Blessed art thou; and the earth that is honoured to enfold thy corse; and the visitor who directeth himself towards thy shrine, and visiteth thy grave; and the one who uttereth thy praise, and proclaimeth that which befell thee during the days of thy Lord. I testify that on thine account the Divine Lote Tree hath lamented, while the hearts of all who, in the days of God, the Possessor of the Throne on high and of Earth below, renounced the world, and turned unto the Supreme Horizon, have melted. Thus hath the Pen spoken in the Spot wherein the King of Eternity is stablished upon His mighty throne. Glory, peace, praise and spirit rest upon thee, thou through whom the tale of Husayn hath been retold, and on whose account the Virgin hath lamented, and the Prophet hath been plunged into conspicuous grief. Fie upon a people who denied thy right, and who cast aside that whereunto they had been commanded by God, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise. The Glory that appeared and shone forth on that first dawn whereon God revealed Himself unto all the dwellers of His Realm of Glory and of His Heavenly Kingdom, and unto the choicest among His creatures, rest upon thee, O thou King of Fidelity, and My Twin Names Há' and Há'! Of you both doth My Supreme Pen testify that ye turned your faces, and directed yourselves, towards God, the Creator of the Heavens, on a day when the stars fell from heaven, the sun was darkened, the trumpet-blast was sounded, and the mountains flowed. Blessed be whoever directeth himself towards you; attaineth the honour of commemorating you; layeth hold upon the cord of your love; and dissociateth himself from all who, without the authority of any clear proof or Book, rose up against you. The first salutation that was uttered by the Tongue of Grandeur ere the creation of earth and heaven be upon thee, O thou Name Há', thou who shinest above the horizon of fidelity. I testify that thou didst direct thyself towards God; didst hear the Call; didst answer "Yea!" unto the Possessor of all Names; and wast so transported by the rapture born of the Divine Verses that thou didst offer up thine all, thy family and thy spirit, in the path of God, the Help in Peril, the All-Glorious, the Self-Subsisting. *

*Tablet of Visitation*

* He is God *

O My Supreme Pen! Make Thou mention of My Name Hasan, who sacrificed himself in My path, and expended all that he possessed for the love of My beauty, and in his longing to meet Me. Make then mention of My Name Husayn, who returned not from the place of sacrifice. Through them both the tale of the Sacrifice (Ishmael) hath been retold, and all hearts have been consumed. Make then mention of Kázim, who beheld that which none of Thy servants hath beheld. I testify that ye believed in God on the day when commotions seized all the peoples of the earth; when the hearts trembled; and when the eyes stared up in terror. I testify that through you the standards of remembrance have been hoisted among all peoples, and the ensigns of guidance have been planted in most lands. It is ye by reason of whose agony the Divine Lote Tree hath lamented; the Rock (Peter) hath cried out; and the mountains have been scattered in dust. Blessed be whoever draweth nigh unto you; is honoured to visit you; and uttereth that which the Pen of the Most High hath spoken in your remembrance and praise, and concerning all that ye were in the love of God, the Lord of the Beginning and the End.

*Tablet of Visitation for the Martyrs of the Land of Sád*

*Do thou, O My Name, who gazest upon My Countenance, when thou beholdest the whiteness of the city wherein the Sun of Fidelity hath set, halt, and say:*

O Land of Sád! Where are the dawning-places of thy light, and the daysprings of thy glory? Where is the adornment of thy temple, and where they through whom the horizon of guidance was illumined amongst Thy creatures? Where are the letters of the Book of God, the Almighty, the All-Praised? O Land of Sád! Where are thy standards and thy signs? Where thy clear tokens, thine ensigns? Have the evidences of tyranny in thee been erased, or doth it continue as of yore? Tell me, nor be of them that hold their peace! Doth the She-Serpent hiss in thee, and doth the Wolf howl as he howled aforetime? Thy Lord, verily, asketh, and Himself maketh reply. He, verily, is the Omnipotent, the All-Powerful. We testify that in thee the treasures of fidelity have been laid up; the Crimson Ark hath foundered; and the She-Camel of God, the Lord of all worlds, hath been hamstrung. The suns of love and fidelity have vanished from thine horizons by reason of that which the hands of those who disbelieved in God, the Gracious, the Most High, have wrought. Say: O Land of Sád! We, verily, commend unto thy care My trust, nay rather My trusts. We ask thee of the flame of hatred: hath its blazing and raging been extinguished? Tell me truly for the sake of God, the Lord of the Exalted Throne!

*O My Name, O thou who speakest forth My praise! Know thou that it behoveth whosoever wisheth to be illumined by the light of immortality, and to attain the honour of visiting one of the people of Bahá', who are established upon the Crimson Ark, and have turned their faces unto the Supreme Horizon, to purify his heart with the water of detachment; to sanctify his countenance from turning unto whatsoever hath been created in the universe, or fashioned in the realm of God's invention; and to be in such a state of consecration that the Kingdom shall be before his face, and all else save God in his rear. Let him then walk with the dignity of God, and His tranquillity, and, with every step he taketh, say with quintessential lowliness and unsurpassed humility:*

O my God! I have purposed to visit them whose blood was spilled in Thy path, and who laid down their lives in Thy love.

*So let him continue until he reacheth the Most Holy Tomb and the Sanctified Dust; let him then halt, and, having gazed to the right, as one might gaze who awaited the mercy of God, the Help in Peril, the Self-Subsisting, turn unto the burial place, and say:*

The first harbinger of salvation that shone forth from the horizon of bounty; and the first fragrance that wafted from the raiment of the Revealer of His Holiness the Lord of Eternity; and the first remembrance that was uttered in the world by the Tongue of the Primal Will; and the first light whereby the hearts of the nations were enraptured, be upon you, O ye the temples of praise, the dawning-places of names, and the daysprings of God's Command in the kingdom of creation. I testify that because of you the All-Merciful mounted the throne of this contingent world; the ocean of forgiveness surged; the stream of living water overflowed; the kingdom of utterance appeared; and the sun of knowledge shone resplendent above the horizon. Ye it is through whose allegiance the Primal Will and its sovereignty have been made manifest; and the Primal Purpose and its potency, and the Primal Destiny and whatsoever hath been decreed therein by God, the Almighty, the Most Powerful, have been disclosed. Through you the Word hath encompassed all; the breeze hath wafted; and mankind hath been illumined by the splendours of a Light that rose and shone forth from the Dayspring of God's Light. Through you, verily, the Dove of Fidelity hath warbled in the Most Sublime Paradise; the Sadratu'l-Muntahá hath spoken; the Nightingale of Bahá' hath poured forth its song; and all things have cried out proclaiming that whereunto God Himself hath testified, He Who is your Maker, your Fashioner, your King, your Origin, your Creator, your Quickener, your Slayer, your Beginning, your End, your Manifester, your Inspirer, your Confirmer, and the Blazoner of your names. Ye are the letters of the Primal Word, the first adornment in the kingdom of creation, and the manifestations of justice in the Most Exalted Realm of Glory. Ye are the Written Book, the Illustrious Symbol, the Outspread Roll, the Frequented Fane. Through you the ensigns of justice have been hoisted, and the standards of victory planted; and through you the fragrance of the Divine raiment hath been wafted, and the sign of sanctity made manifest. Through you the gates of bounty have been flung open before the nations, and the loving-kindness of the All-Merciful hath rained down from the heaven of understanding. Blessed are ye; and all who seek through you to draw nigh unto God; and all who lay fast hold upon the hem of your garment, cleave tenaciously unto your cord, and speak forth your praise. Woe unto all such as deny your right, turn away from you, show pride towards you, and dispute the Divine providence manifested in you. All things testify unto your glory, the exaltation of your station, and the gain ye have secured both in this world and in the next; likewise unto the loss of those who disbelieved in God when he came with resplendent signs, clear tokens and effulgent lights. Glory be unto Thee, O Thou through Whose Name they who adore Thy unity have soared into the atmosphere of Thy nearness and Thy presence, and they who are devoted to Thee have hastened unto the place of sacrifice for love of Thee, and for the sake of Thy pleasure. I ask Thee, by them who have suffered martyrdom in Thy path, and who were so transported by the rapture born of Thy Divine Verses that naught on earth could prevent them from drawing nigh unto Thee, to write down for us with Thy Pen of Glory that which will profit us both in this world and in the next. O my God, my Master, and my Hope! I ask thee by this purest dust, and by this sacred tomb, to forgive me, and to pardon my grievous trespasses. Do Thou ordain for me, by Thy grace, that whereby mine eye shall be gladdened, and my breast dilated. Potent art Thou to do what pleaseth Thee. In Thy grasp are the keys of mercy and salvation. There is no God but Thee, the All-Powerful, the All-Compelling, the Almighty.

A Tablet of Visitation was also revealed by the pen of His Holiness 'Abdu'l-Bahá -- exalted be His praise -- in honour of the Twin Shining Lights, and of Áqá Mírzá Mihdí Ikhvánu's-Safá, who was subsequently buried in the vicinity of the resting-place of the Twin Shining Lights.

The wording of the Blessed Tablet of Visitation is as follows.

*His most sweet utterance:*

O friends! Do ye on behalf of 'Abdu'l-Bahá go one day especially to visit that luminous spot, and recite these words: "The glory shining from the apex of exaltation, and the light beaming from the Concourse on High, descend upon, and surround, that luminous spot, wherein lie buried those stars of radiant splendour, the twin glistening lights in the Abhá Kingdom; and the refulgent lamp in the globe of piety, and detached spirit guiding unto the way of truth. I testify that ye are the signs of guidance amidst mankind, the ensigns of the Abhá Kingdom, and the kings of the throne of supreme bestowal. Blessed are ye, inasmuch as ye attained this most sublime station, and loftiest pinnacle, and were raised up by God unto an exalted station of truth. I, verily, seek the blessing of this perfumed dust and fragrant musk, for it formeth the resting-places of those well-assured and contented souls who are nigh unto the Lord of mankind. I ask God to make your graves niches of light in this perspicuous age and glorious century -- my Lord doth, verily, single out for His mercy whomsoever He willeth -- in order that the sincere may derive therefrom illumination, and the visitors inhale therefrom the breaths of flowers." The Glory of Glories rest upon you. 'Abdu'l-Bahá 'Abbás

Section Four

Blessed Tablets

Revealed by the Pen of

The Ancient Beauty,

Exalted be His Glory

For the Twin Shining Lights

Upon them be the Glory

of the Most Glorious

**
*Blessed Tablet in Honour of the Beloved of Martyrs***

He is the Glorious, the Most Glorious

O thou Name of God! Hearken unto the sweet melodies of the Spirit, and take no heed of them who have disbelieved in God and His Verses, and who have turned against His Cause. Follow thou the Faith of the Spirit in the love of thy Lord: this is the root of religion, though none shall know it save all that are well-assured and discern aright. Say: O people! The veils of idle fancy have been torn away; the heaven of impiety hath been cleft asunder; and God hath come down upon the cloud of holiness, surrounded by a host of angels. Thereupon all things were changed; every soul was shaken; and every proud and lofty peak was reduced in dust. Remain thou steadfast in the Cause through the power of God and His might; and assume thou in this state a seat of conspicuous glory. Assist then the Cause to the extent that thou art able, for the people of the Bayán would fain return the Cause unto the abyss where they themselves are fallen. Lay hold upon the reins of the Cause lest the fingers of impiety profane it: this is that which hath been destined for thee in His glorious and preserved Tablets. We have decreed that every soul should write touching this Cause that whereby the feet of them who are endued with understanding shall be confirmed in an exalted honour. O Khalíl! Shatter thou the idols of imagination through the power of thy Lord; then lead out the people from the darkness of passion, and usher them into an abode of safety beneath the shadow of the Divine Lote Tree that hath sprung up in truth from beside a mighty throne. Beware lest aught distract thee; do thou of thine own accord draw nigh unto God, Who created thee, fashioned thee, and appointed thee to be a glorious remembrance unto His servants. Shouldst thou wish to learn what hath touched the Beauty of an Effulgent Glory, know that He hath fallen into the well of envy: here is His raiment, bespattered with His blood, which we have sent unto thee that thou mayest have clear proof of Our claim. Thus have we inspired thee, and revealed unto thee what befell the Manifestation of the Self of God at the hands of His servants who, though created by a mere indication of His purpose, as articulated by His pen, dealt frowardly towards their Lord. Be thou the Word of God, and the Sword of His Command among His servants, that through thee He may distinguish between those who believed in God and His Verses, and those who disbelieved and rebelled against the Cause. Take heed that thou aid thy Lord at all times, and approach not those from whom thou inhalest the odour of animosity towards this Youth, Who hath shone forth above the Dawning-place of Eternity with manifest dominion. Say: O people! If ye believed in 'Alí because of the revelation to Him of the Bayán; and before Him in Muhammad because of the revelation to Him of the Furqán; and again in the One Who conversed with God (Moses) because of the revelation to Him of the Torah, then by the righteousness of God these are their selfsame Verses, which, in this peerless form, have been sent down from the throne on high. These apart, the whole earth hath been filled with the evidences of a sovereignty that hath encompassed all the worlds. Be ye then abashed, O people, before God, Who created you by His command; and repent ye for having failed in your duty towards Him -- a duty that is owed here, did ye but know it. Say: Blind are the eyes that will not turn towards His court; and mute is the tongue that will not celebrate the wonders of His praise; and deaf are the ears that will not hearken unto the sweet melodies of the Spirit uttered by this tongue, which proclaimeth in all things: "I, in very truth, am God: no God is there but Him; His knowledge, truly, embraceth all things." Say: O people! Cast away that which ye possess. Take hold, then, of the Tablet of God with a power born of Him, and inhale its savour: should ye discover therefrom the fragrance of the All-Merciful, guard it from the blight of demons. Then assist Him so far as lieth in your power: He, verily, assisteth His loved ones as He pleaseth; and verily His assistance is nigh unto the believers. Beware that ye dispute not with God; nor contend with the One Who is His own Self; nor repudiate that whereby your names shall be exalted, and the truth of your own religion hath been established. Fear God, and be not distant from the shore of nearness. The Spirit be upon thee, and upon all who follow thy Lord's command at even and at morn. It is complete: revealed a second time from the Abhá Kingdom by Our Name Há'.

*Blessed Tablet in Honour of the King of Martyrs*

He is the Glorious, the Most Glorious

From the Burning Bush beyond the Radiant City upon the hallowed Spot of God's Command, the Mystery of God hath, by the power of the spirit, been witnessed, and speaketh in truth saying: "O people of the Bayán! Have ye disbelieved in the One through Whom ye believed in God aforetime? Here is My Beauty, which hath been revealed through His grace; yet have ye allowed them that are the manifestations of names in the kingdom of creation to shut you out therefrom; notwithstanding that they were all created by His Word. He, verily, is powerful over all things." O Most Great Name! We, verily, have made thee to be among the greatest of names, that thou mayest issue forth from the abode of silence, and rise above the dawning-place of utterance to proclaim a Cause that hath encompassed all worlds. Unloose therefore thy tongue in truth, and announce unto the people that whereof, by the power of the Spirit, He hath informed thee in this Tablet, which was sent down from the right hand of the throne. Beware lest aught deter thee from commemorating thy Lord. Burn away the veils of sorrows through the Name of thy Lord, the God of Mercy; then shine forth above the horizon of remembrance with a perspicuous light. Beware lest thou forget the occasion when thou didst enter into the Beatific Spot, and didst come before the throne; when We cheered thee with tidings of all good, and ordained for thee on earth an exalted station. Break not the Covenant thou didst enter into before God, neither violate His Testament, but be steadfastly loyal to thine undertaking. Be constant in thy love for thy Lord: beware lest thou withhold thyself from that which We have destined for thee, that thou mayest be reckoned in the Mother Tablet among such as are well grounded in their belief. Write then in vindication of this Cause whatsoever the Spirit infuseth into thy breast; He, verily, will inspire thee with the truth, and assist thee in a matter whose outcome hath been predetermined by the Pen of God. Spirit, Honour and Glory be upon thee, and upon those who are with thee at the dawning of the Cause; at the eventide of holiness; and at every moment. To be delivered unto Al-Hasan An-Nahrí of the dwellers of Sád, that he may be of them that do good.

*In the Name of God, the Exalted, in His All-Highest Station*

O thou Letter of Fidelity! Thy missive hath arrived before Us; I am cognizant of all thou didst write therein; and We have accepted thine expressions of love for God, for the Manifestations of His Self, and the Mirrors of His Being. Erelong shall God requite thee with a most excellent reward from Him, and shall cause thy name to be recorded in the Book of the Spirit among the rightly guided. Even now doth He exhort thee with the counsels of eternity, and assist thee in words of holiness to grasp the essence of the Cause, that thou mayest inhale the fragrances of Paradise wafting from the Beauteous City, and abide with Divine honour in the Immortal Garden for evermore. Exercise discernment in thine affairs; defame no one; follow not thy passions; and place thy trust in God, thy Lord. Walk then upon the earth with a dignity born of God; shun those in whose hearts thou perceivest resentment towards God and His loved ones; and enter not into disputation with the unbelievers. Shouldst thou act as We have inspired thee, thou shalt discover on earth a prosperity vouchsafed of God; and in the world to come a yet goodlier station and more excellent estate. Thus have We revealed unto thee the Word of Truth; taught thee the paths of guidance; and made known unto thee the ways of godliness, that thou mayest discern clearly the nature of the Cause. Say: O people! Fear God, and follow not the steps of demons. Believe ye all that God hath sent down unto you; then follow whatsoever this Servant imparteth unto you of the sweet melodies of eternity, that ye may be of them that champion the Cause in thronéd heights. Relate unto thy heart this vision touching all that We have unveiled to thee of the mysteries of destiny from beyond the Crimson City. Thus hath God's sentence been irrevocably passed upon all people. Rejoice then in thy spirit inasmuch as We have answered thee, and made mention of thee, in this Tablet, and ordained for thee a great glad tidings on the part of God. Revealed from the Há' after the Bá', Yá Hasan!

*Blessed Tablet Revealed in Honour of the King of Martyrs*

He is God

Glory be to Thee, O Lord my God! O my God! Verily, this is Thy servant who hath been carried away by the heat of Thy love and the transports of Thy devotion, and upon whom have wafted the breaths of Thy holiness and the melodies of Thy spirit. Such was the exultation at Thy beauty, and the ecstasy at Thy glory, engendered in his heart that he became detached from all things and from the suggestions of all people; until he journeyed through Thee unto Thee, and emigrated from Thee even unto Thyself. The way was barred until he entered the paths of Thy loving-kindness. It was as though he walked in his own person, so great was his yearning to meet Thee; that he might arrive at the gate of the City of Thy Oneness, and attain the glorious seats of Thine Eternity. At length he stood before the Tabernacles of Thine Exaltation and the Canopy of Thy Majesty in the Habitation of Holiness in the shelter of the Sanctuary of Thy Grandeur, the Garden of Thy Beauty and the City of Thy Guidance; and attained, through that surpassing honour and superlative distinction, unto a state wherein the cord of his servitude was strengthened by the fibre of Thy Lordship, and the lamp of his poverty was kindled by the wicks of Thy riches. Thereupon he entered into the depths of the oceans of the Divine Essence before the surging of the Verses of Thy glorious sovereignty. Unto Thee be praise, therefore, O my God, for whatsoever Thou hast bestowed upon him by Thy bounty, and honoured him withal by Thy power; and unto Thee be thanks for all Thou hast sustained him withal of the gems of hidden favours, and the wonders of his treasured mercy, which have come to fruition upon the trees of love in the inmost realities of hearts. I ask Thee, then, O my God, to cause him to hearken unto the call of this Firebird in this Abhá Paradise, that with his whole being he may come forth for the sake of establishing Thy victory in the kingdom of Thy creation and in the dominion of Thy glory; and that his spirit may be purified from all that hath not been ordained by Thy decree, nor enjoyeth the sanction of Thy good pleasure: forasmuch as Thou holdest in Thy hands the reins of all things. Thou, verily, art the Revealer of the Revelation, Who singest upon the supernal Light within the Sinaitic Tree; and Thou, indeed, hast power over all things. Bless Thou, O Lord my God, Thy First Light whereby the spirits of Thy sacred eternality have soared aloft; and bless Thou moreover Thy Mansion that moveth upon the air in the very axis of the sun, the centre of Thine appointment at Thy pleasure by Thy decree; and all those that guide thereunto in the lofty heights of eternity, and in the bowers of the invisible realm. Thou, truly, art the Ordainer, the All-Compelling, the All-Conquering, the All-Knowing, the Ever-Living, the Almighty, the All-Glorious, the All-Powerful, the All-Informed. Array then with a robe of blessing woven of the cotton of immortality the temple of him who is thy brother in the world of being; and convey from me to him a salutation from the pages of fidelity; likewise to all that are about thee of the people of guidance. 251, The Land of Sád, Há' Sín-Yá' Nún

*Blessed Tablet Revealed in Honour of the King of Martyrs*

He is God, the Almighty, All-Powerful

In these days it is natural that selfish passions should have prevented some from observing justice and equity, and whatsoever hath been sent down in the Tablets concerning unity and harmony. Even so, what is the Pen of the Most High to say, and to whose behoof should the Tongue of Knowledge speak? The ignorance of God's creatures hath darkened the resplendent horizon of knowledge; the heedlessness of the people hath veiled the radiant dawn of guidance. In most of the Divinely-revealed Tablets We have enjoined upon all wisdom, unity, laudable deeds and a praiseworthy character. Though all have read these, and become aware of the Divine precepts, yet have they remained far distant from the Straight Path, and given precedence rather to their own desires. We have enjoined upon them unity; rather have they risen up in strife. We have summoned them unto wisdom; rather have they shown forth the reverse. In most of the Tablets they have been forbidden to direct themselves towards the Divine Court; this notwithstanding, each day a host arriveth and another host departeth. There is no power nor strength except in God! Ye have heard of the developments in the Land of Tá', and the determination of some to commit a heinous act. We have commanded all souls to set the world in order; rather have they occupied themselves with sowing strife. Methinks they have regarded the Divine commands as of no account, and considered the Lordly precepts as mere fancies. They speak as passion moveth them, then attribute what they say unto the One True God. He, verily, is clear of those who have wrought mischief in the land after it had been set in order, and who speak that which hath been forbidden them in the Book of God, the Lord of the worlds. Please God, in training certain weak souls, and in promoting concord and union, thou must, so far as thou art able, exert an unremitting effort, that haply they may attain unto that which God hath purposed. The sorrow of this Wronged One is clear and manifest from this Tablet. Verily, we are God's, and unto Him shall we return. 251, Sád, Há' Sín Nún

*Blessed Tablet of the Most Holy Abhá Beauty in Honour of the King of Martyrs, Containing an Exhortation to Teach the Cause*

*His honour Há' before Sín, upon him be the Glory of God*

In the Name of Him Who speaketh with unerring wisdom

Há' Sín. Praise be to God, thou didst inhale the fragrance of the Divine raiment, and it guided thee unto the dawning-place of the Hidden Secret, and the dayspring of the Well-guarded Treasure: wherefore at length, on the wings of yearning and devotion, of rapture and attraction, thou didst set out to reach the Most Exalted Destination, traversing prairies, deserts, seas and mountains, until thou didst attain the Furthermost Bourne, and the Spot around which the Concourse on High circle in adoration. No station equalleth this station: thereto have testified the Books of God aforetime and hereafter, and withal this perspicuous and mighty Tablet. Thy letters were received, and all were graced with an attentive hearing. Praise be to God, thou art occupied in remembrance of Him Who is the Beloved of the World, and steadfast in service to the Cause. I swear by the Sun of the horizon of sanctity that this utterance, which hath risen above the dayspring of the Pen of the All-Merciful, shall never be blotted out from the pages of the world. Do thou recognize its station, and be of the thankful. Please God, those souls who have fixed their gaze upon the Most Sublime Horizon, and laid fast hold upon the hem of the mercy of the Incomparable Friend, should, in teaching the Divine Cause, do so both with wisdom and with utterance. All matters today are dependent upon wisdom. Should wisdom not dictate it, it is not permitted to speak. All must cleave unto such matters as are conducive to the assurance and tranquillity of the people, for by reason of the clamour of the heedless the hearts of the weak are like to be sore shaken. Thy Lord, verily, is the Compassionate, the All-Bountiful. Blessed is the one who aideth his Lord with goodly deeds and a spiritual character; he, truly, is reckoned among the people of Bahá' in the Crimson Book, wherein the Pen of the Most High hath inscribed the secrets of all that hath been and shall be. Wondrous and incomparable Verses have been sent down especially for thee. Please God, thou mayest attain unto them all, and, with perfect wisdom and eloquence, engage in service to the Cause -- service such as will be permanent and lasting, to the degree that the evanescence of the world and all its vicissitudes shall never change it. Teaching is the Divine command, provided it be undertaken with wisdom. He, verily, speaketh the truth; leadeth the way; and revealeth the proof. There is none other God but Him, the Almighty, the Beauteous. 251

These pearl-like words were revealed from the Pen of the Ancient Beauty for his honour Há' and Sín.

*His exalted Utterance:*

O Há' before Sín! The Greater Branch hath come into Our presence, and spoken in praise of thee. I beseech the One True God to assist thee in that which shall be the means and cause of the continuation of thine existence. Praise be to God, thou hast quaffed of the life-giving waters that have flowed out from the Pen of the All-Merciful, and hast hearkened unto the rustling of the leaves of the Divine Lote Tree. This mention of thee, and this loving-kindness, shall abide and endure so long as the Kingdom of God shall endure. Erelong shall there be made manifest all that hath flowed forth from the Pen of the Most High. We ask God to aid thee in preserving this most exalted station; He, verily, is the Almighty, the Ancient of Days. Under all conditions thy name hath been, and is, remembered. This is a token of thy Lord's bounty unto thee. *Finis*.

The following Blessed Tablet was revealed by the Pen of the Ancient Beauty -- exalted be His glory -- in honour of the King of Martyrs ere the latter's martyrdom.

*His exalted Utterance:*

In the Name of the All-Knowing Expounder. The ocean of true knowledge streaming from the dayspring of the mouth of the Will of Him Who is the All-Merciful hath revealed its splendour in the form of these words. The clouds of the idle fancies of the ignorant have made dark and gloomy the world's luminous horizon; while the tyranny of the rulers hath rendered turbid the clear fount of tranquillity. Yet the day is approaching when the Divine decrees will have penetrated these intervening veils, and dissipated these various impediments and obstacles. Say: O friends! What need is there for consternation, what cause for fear? Never hath there been, nor is there now, any doubt that all who are endowed with spirit shall one day be overtaken, and seized upon, by death. Such being the case, if this death be converted into martyrdom, and take place in the path of God, it would assuredly be preferable. Every intelligent and thinking person will testify that this station hath ever been, and ever shall be, the loftiest of all stations. All men are commanded to observe wisdom, and forbidden to engage in mischief, strife and contention; yet should aught befall, then with perfect resignation must they direct their steps unto the scene of sacrifice in the path of the Incomparable Friend. I swear by the Sun of the horizon of sanctity! Should a soul quaff from the cup of knowledge the crystal waters of the love of the All-Merciful, never would he be moved by the wrong of the oppressor and the onslaught of the tyrant even to sadness, how much less to fear and consternation! Please God, thou wilt acquaint all the wayfarers in the Straight Path with that which hath been sent down in this Tablet from the Pen of the All-Merciful, so that, with the utmost joy and gladness, they may be occupied with the remembrance of Him Who is the Lord of all men. Say: The Pen of the Most High affirmeth: the death of each soul is predetermined in the Book of God, neither shall it be advanced or delayed by a single moment. Is it then seemly that the lover should shrink from meeting his Beloved, or be sorrowed by the prospect of laying down his life in the pathway of the Adored One? Nay, by Myself, the True One! And yet the people for the most part apprehend it not. Say: Sanctify and purify the hearts, that they may discover a window giving onto the Most Great Ocean: thereafter neither the hosts of the world, nor the clamours of the champions of the nations, shall have the power to keep such souls back from Him Who is the King of Eternity. Do thou then beseech God graciously to confirm and assist them in such wise that they may soar up on the wings of longing unto God, the Supreme King, the All-Knowing, the All-Informed. We, verily, have made mention of thee aforetime, and in this wondrous Tablet, that thou mayest be well assured of the grace of thy Lord, and mayest relate unto the people that which hath proceeded from His Most Holy, His All-Glorious, and His Most Exalted Pen. The Glory of God rest upon thee, and upon all those who have held fast unto the commandments of God, the Lord of all worlds.

*
*

Section Five

Tablets Revealed after the Ascension

Of the Twin Shining Lights

In the Name of Other believers

Concerning the Station of the Martyrs of Isfahán

**
**

*Tá', His honour Zaynu'l-'Ábidín, who attained unto Thee*

He is the Most Holy, the Most Mighty, the Witness, the Seer, the All-Informed

A remembrance from Us unto him who attained the presence of this Wronged One when He was fallen into the hands of the heedless. I bear witness that he set out from his home, proceeding in the direction of the Frequented Fane and Blessed Station which the All-Merciful hath sent down in the Furqán, and attained unto that which he desired on the Day of God, the Lord of the worlds. The servant in attendance is at hand, and hath recited once again thy letter as a bounty on the part of God, the Almighty, the All-Praised. Blessed be thy tongue for telling forth that which hath befallen the Daystar of Bathá (Mecca), for whom the Celestial Concourse, and the inmates of Paradise in their noble habitation, have lamented. Blessed is he who extolleth the names of Há' and Há', and thereafter of him that was named Kázim, who laid down his life in the way of God, the Lord of the Day of Reckoning. I testify that neither martial hosts, nor the clamour of every wayward cleric, overawed him. By My life! We, verily, found him steadfast in the Cause of his Lord, in such wise that the inmates of Paradise, and those who circle the throne as bidden by Him Who is the All-Glorious, the Most Great, were filled with wonder. Erelong shall God reveal unto him that which hath been hidden from the face of His servants; He, verily is the Incomparable, the All-Knowing. By the righteousness of God! They attained that which none had previously attained; thereto testifieth My Pen of Glory in this wondrous Tablet. From this Spot We salute thee, and all those who have attained unto the choice wine of steadfastness in this Cause, whereby the hearts of the learned have trembled, and the feet of the wise have slipped.

*To be favoured by the purest and most luminous glances of the respected and revered Afnán, his honour Áqá Siyyid Mím -- upon him be of all glories the Most Glorious*

In the Name of the One All-Seeing, All-Knowing God

The quintessence of glorification and praise beseemeth that Ancient King and Possessor of the world Who, through but a single effulgence of the resplendent lights of His beauty, seated Abraham amid the fire, and sent Ishmael unto the place of sacrifice. The mind is perplexed to conceive what the nature of this effulgence might be. If it fall upon a sovereign he giveth up his kingdom; if it shed its splendour upon a complete pauper, he becometh contemptuous of the world of riches; and if it turn upon the embodiment of riches, he forgoeth his station, and standeth in the ranks of servants, ready to offer service. I swear by the ocean of Divine knowledge that were He to make manifest that which He hath concealed, thou wouldst see the whole world turn into Abrahams, and into the Ishmaels of the age; howbeit this company of Abrahams would not consent unto the transmutation of the fire; neither would this company of Ishmaels return from the place of sacrifice. This evanescent servant is at a loss what to say, and what to represent. He is at once bewildered and forbidden to speak. Such being the case, he can but cling unto the cord of "Increase my bewilderment in Thee!" Gracious God! A single Call at once bringeth intoxication and bestoweth clarity of thought! It at once bringeth forgetfulness and conferreth the knowledge of all things! Would I were permitted to recount what I have seen and known! The matter lieth solely in His hand; unto none belongeth any station, jurisdiction, power, or strength save by His leave and His bounty. May my spirit be a ransom for thy remembrance, and a sacrifice for thine arising. In the days when the Mansion had become the Most Sublime Vision, his honour the Name of God Mím Há' -- upon him be of all glories the Most Glorious -- arrived one day at sunset, and attained unto the Most Holy Court. Thereafter he handed to this servant an envelope containing both thine own distinguished autograph and the letter from his honour Áqá Mírzá Ismá'íl. That same evening, circumstances so demanded that this servant found occasion to present their whole contents before the Countenance of the Ancient Beauty; and when the recitation was complete He arose from His seat, began to pace, and said: "O My Afnán! Blessed are ye, inasmuch as ye have been favoured with the loving-kindness of your Lord, and been honoured to recognize Him, and to turn towards Him; and blessed are they that love you for the sake of God, the Lord of the worlds. We, verily, have exalted your stations. Erelong shall ye behold them: to this will testify whoso turneth towards My Face, recognizeth My Most Mighty Cause, and hasteneth unto My Straight Path. O My Afnán, in most of the Tablets mention hath been made of the greatness of the Cause. By the righteousness of God! Greater is it than every great thing! Were anyone to reflect upon the stations of that soul who, in this day, is graciously aided to recognize the Cause of God, he would in general become acquainted with the greatness of the Cause. Thy Lord, truly, unlocketh the door of understanding before the face of whom He will; He, verily, is the Supreme Ordainer, the All-Knowing. O My Afnán! The loving-kindness of the One True God hath been, and evermore shall be, with you. Consider ye this utterance that shone forth from the Dayspring of the Revelation of the All-Merciful unto one of those who had turned their faces towards Him. 'O Husayn, cleave thou unto this blessed Word, which is even as an ark upon the ocean of the knowledge of Him Who is the King of creation. Although this Word is ancient -- meaning that the Manifestations of the Cause spake it of old -- yet today is it made manifest in a wondrous new attire, inasmuch as the true Isráfíl hath breathed a fresh spirit of meaning into the temples of words. It is this: "Whoso is for God, God is for him." Shouldst thou voyage upon this ocean, thou wouldst behold thyself endowed with a new spirit and a boundless assurance; wouldst soar on the wings of ardent longing into the atmosphere of the love of Him Who is the Daystar of the world; and wouldst, with perfect joy, gladness and contentment, walk upon this straight path of justice.' O Afnán! Ye have turned unto the True One -- meaning that ye have been assisted by His grace to attain unto this station -- and the True One likewise, with the utmost loving-kindness, turneth unto you. Let it not be imagined that the fruits of this loving-kindness shall remain hidden. Nay, by Mine own Self! Erelong shall God make them manifest on earth: He, verily, is your Friend and your Helper; He, verily, is the Ever-Forgiving, the Most Merciful. These are the days of the Revelation, and the grace vouchsafed is boundless. He, verily, is the Most Gracious; He, verily, is the Most Bountiful; He, verily, is the Most Generous. Under all conditions have ye regard for wisdom, and put your reliance in the True One. In His hand is the preservation of all things; He, verily, is the Almighty, the Most Powerful. The Glory of God rest upon you, and upon whoso loveth you, and upon whoso setteth his face towards you, and hearkeneth unto your call and your remembrance. He, verily, is of them that have won the gracious favour of their Lord, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise." Finis.

As for what thou didst write concerning his honour Mírzá Ismá'íl, his letter was presented in its entirety. He said: "In some of what he hath mentioned he is right. He should be treated with kindliness and forbearance." A most sublime and holy Tablet was also revealed especially for him from the firmament of Grace, and despatched hence. Do thou o'erlook it, and send it on. Our Lord, truly, is the Ordainer, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise. The aforenamed Mírzá hath however fallen into great perplexity. Although he is right in asserting that the Cause is great, inasmuch as it is related unto God, yet were he to immerse himself a while in the ocean of awareness he would perceive that it is, and ever shall be, the finest, the greatest, the truest, the most perfect, and the most exalted of all matters in the world. At the time when this evanescent servant was in 'Iráq, the martyred Twin Shining Lights set out for Zawrá' (Baghdád) with the purpose of visiting the Divine Kaaba. On their return from the Land of Taff (Karbilá) they attained unto the Most Holy Court; and, after hearkening unto the Call of God, they underwent in reality a transformation. The loving-kindness shown towards them, unknown as they were amongst the people, was so remarkable that some were astonished at it, and marvelled greatly. Thereafter they, pursuant to the Divine behest, returned again to their own land; the Hand of Divine power raised them up and arrayed them with the robe of honour; and from the cloud of bounty blessings rained down upon them, until they became known and celebrated throughout the world in the name of the Ancient King, and in truth He established their place firmly in the hearts, even as thou hast seen and dost now witness. Subsequent to their return to the Land of Sád, two letters came from them to the Most Holy Court, and likewise other letters. Therein, with utmost lowliness and ardour, they craved, and expressed the hope of attaining, the very station which afterwards they won. What greater bounty is there than this, that, praise be to God, in the nether world they were identified with the name of the True One, it being observed that even the ungodly behaved with deference in their presence; while at the end of their days they attained a station whose description is beyond aught that the pen of this servant could compass, or the tongue of this evanescent one express? From the Tablets that have come down from the heaven of the Will of the Lord of all men concerning this supreme calamity, the full measure of this station may be known and ascertained. O beloved of mine heart! A hundred thousand blessings be theirs, and a hundred thousand regrets the portion of this servant! Methinks, with the tongues of the whole world he exclaimeth at all times: "Would I had been with them!" Observe thou that the Prince of the World was martyred under the circumstances that have reached thy blessed ears, while these are accounted among His servants. Yet observably the effect of their martyrdom is greater, its influence more complete, and its pain more searing. Exalted be He Who raised them up. Exalted be He Who honoured them. Exalted be He Who caused them to win this station, in striving after which God's chosen ones have offered up their lives.

I swear by the Beloved of the world that never shall his regret on this account fade from the heart of this servant. I ask Him, exalted is He, graciously to assist me to do His will and pleasure. He, verily, is the Almighty, the Most Powerful. As for your having referred matters unto the True One, and committed them to His care, in this regard He said: "They, indeed, have done well! Their Lord, the God of Mercy, is, verily, the All-Knowing, the All-Informed. He revealeth whatsoever He pleaseth by virtue of His sovereignty. He, verily, is the One Whom naught can frustrate; Whom martial hosts cannot affright; and Whom neither the tyranny of the mighty nor the ascendancy of the powerful can weaken. He, verily, ordaineth what He willeth, and doeth as He pleaseth." Finis.

Another Tablet was graciously revealed in honour of the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs.

That which hath been witnessed in this Most Great Revelation is such that no room for doubt or misgiving hath been, or is now, left for anyone, save those who are actuated by perversity and speak with complete and palpable injustice. Whatsoever was revealed beforehand in the Divine Tablets touching subsequent events hath been set forth explicitly and without allusion. Should anyone look into the Tablets of Fu'ád and Ra'ís, the Lawh-i-Párís, and the rest of the Tablets that were revealed amid the rigours of the Prison and the subsequent opening of its gates, he would be filled with wonder and amazement. Letter by letter everything hath come to pass. After the revelation of each of these Tablets, the hearts of some, though well assured, were yet astonished to conceive how these matters could come about. This servant was wont to observe, "They shall see." One day this servant inquired, "Were the Chief to repent, might he be graced with the robe of forgiveness?" Thereupon the Countenance of the Ancient of Days turned towards me, and He said: "I swear by God, besides Whom there is none other God! All that the Most Merciful hath sent down in the Tablet shall come to pass." Then, in the Persian tongue He affirmed: "Should all the powers of heaven and earth combine with the purpose of altering one single letter of the Lawh-i-Ra'ís, they have never been, nor ever shall be, able to accomplish this." Were anyone to see that Tablet, and to learn of the disasters that befell the Chief, his followers and his lands, assuredly he would cry out betwixt earth and heaven in the name of God, our Exalted and Most Glorious Lord. The people are fast asleep: truly they are sunk in slumber, and in this state shall they remain until such time as they themselves perceive their own levels of the Abyss, meaning their own stations. He likewise bade me, "Write thou unto the Afnán: 'O Afnán! Be not sorrowed by the happenings of the world. From the clouds of His favour, and the heaven of His generosity He bestoweth His bounty as is requisite. If in this supreme calamity some suffer injury or detriment, there hath not been, nor is there now, any harm in this. He, verily, is the Great Giver, the Generous. He bestoweth now as He hath done in the past. If in certain cases a delay occurreth, it is in view of a surpassing wisdom. He, verily, knoweth what shall appear, and within His grasp are held the reins of all things; He, verily, is the Great Giver, the Ever-Forgiving.'" As for the circumstance, related in thy letter, that thou didst write to his honour Áqá Siyyid Ahmad the Afnán -- upon him be of all glories the Most Glorious -- advising him to donate to the expenses of the survivors of the wronged martyr -- upon him be the Light of God and His mercy -- first and foremost, this matter ranketh above all others in the sight of the One True God -- exalted be His glory; yet should it be put into effect only after cognizance is taken of their affairs, and exact information acquired of their circumstances. For if aught be done in secret, and his honour Áqá Mírzá Ismá'íl become apprised thereof, this would assuredly cast him into despair, and perchance occasion ill-feeling between him and the survivors. Thy solicitude for them is greatly beloved in the sight of God. The Tongue of Grandeur speaketh these blessed words: "Well is it with him who inquireth into their circumstances, and setteth right whatsoever is deficient." In truth, this matter is today of enormous moment. Please God, thou and the Afnán will continue your attentions as of yore. As for what thou didst write concerning the claims, accounts and debts of the wronged martyr, this was presented before the Divine Countenance. He said: "Trusting wholly in God, do thou proceed according to the commercial law. After the dues of the branches of the Divine Lote Tree and of the generality of mankind have been settled, it is essential to safeguard and protect the property of the heirs, insofar as this exceedeth not the bounds of wisdom, nor becometh a cause of sorrow and ill-feeling. The owner of the property hath passed out of this nether realm, and all that is therein, and returned unto a station such that the whole world would be powerless to depict the most inconsiderable of its praises. The welfare of the survivors likewise is in the hands of the One True God -- exalted be His estate. He, verily, is the best of advocates and the best of providers. Outwardly, however, there is the matter of reliance upon material means as provided by God, and all are commanded to adhere thereunto. Please God, thou mayest under all conditions be aided and assisted to serve the Cause of God." In truth thou hast borne extraordinary exertions in the path of God, and so likewise his honour Áqá Siyyid Ahmad the Afnán -- upon him be of all glories the Most Glorious. Praise be to God that thou hast attained unto this station for which no peer or parallel could be conceived. It is the station of praise and thanksgiving. Under all conditions this evanescent servant beseecheth his Lord to send down upon thee from the heaven of His grace a mercy from His presence and a bounty from His side. He, verily, is the Great Giver, the Generous. Praise be to God, the Lord of all the worlds.

Another Tablet was graciously revealed from the most pure Pen of the Blessed Beauty in honour of the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs.

O 'Alí! Thy letter which thou didst send unto him who set himself towards My Kingdom, circled around My throne, and attained unto My presence, hath arrived before this Wronged One, and the servant in attendance hath presented it before the throne. Thy Lord, truly, heareth and seeth, and I am the All-Hearing. We have inhaled the fragrance of thy setting thyself, and turning thy face, towards Us, and have remembered thee as a bounty on Our part. His mercy hath surpassed the world. Thy Lord, truly, is the Most Gracious, the All-Bountiful. Please God, with perfect joy and radiance, thou wilt speak forth with perfect wisdom the praise of Him Who is the Beloved of creation, and in all thy affairs fix thy gaze upon the horizon of His good pleasure. The root of the meaning of belief in the unity of God is this, that well-assured souls should under all circumstances direct their eyes exclusively towards the One True God, and move in accordance with His good pleasure. Were any soul in this day to perform every charitable work and goodly deed, yet attain not unto the good pleasure of the True One, assuredly this would bear no fruit. Thus it is that He saith, "Exert yourselves, that ye may attain unto the word indicative of His good pleasure." Do thou exert thyself so that all may attain unto this Most Sublime Station: that they may act for the sake of God; lay hold upon the permission of God; and cleave unto the good pleasure of God. O 'Alí! Do thou meditate upon the Light that shone forth from the Land of Sád. Till now most people have not acquired so much as a sprinkling from the ocean of his understanding. He had attained unto the true martyrdom. By My life! Years passed over him during which he was wholly selfless in the Will of his Lord, and in the Purpose of His Master. In no respect had he any thought, purpose, or will of his own; and at all times did he wait upon the Command of God. Without the leave and permission of the True One he embarked upon no enterprise. For years indeed he had already been a sacrifice in the path of the Beloved, although to outward seeming he spoke, heard, and walked like others. This is the Supreme Sacrifice, the Most Sublime Station, and the Most August Seat; and this exalted and most glorious station was crowned with outward martyrdom. He gleaned the pearls of the ocean of life, and cast them at the feet of the Beloved. Thus it was that he attained unto the Most Great Remembrance, while the Pen of the Most High was for a season occupied with his commemoration, so as to make manifest his work, his station, his rank and his devotion. O 'Alí! He attained unto a twofold martyrdom; and were the former station to be explained in detail, assuredly most people would be astounded. Please God, all the friends may attain unto that which is today beloved. We, verily, remember them in this Tablet, and rejoice them with tidings of the grace of God, and of His mercy that hath surpassed all created things. Say: Arise ye with the most great steadfastness in this Most Glorious and Exalted Cause, through the agency of which the Tongue of Grandeur hath proclaimed: "The Kingdom belongeth unto Him Who is the Possessor of all things visible and invisible!" All must quaff at every moment from the living waters of contentment, forasmuch as they are remembered in the Court of the True One, and their names writ down by the Pen of the Most High. Nor shall the stations of those souls that are well assured, contented, and pleasing unto God, remain hidden. If, pursuant to an inscrutable Divine wisdom, these should for a few days remain hidden, the Hand of Divine power shall assuredly tear away the veil, and make them manifest. Do thou likewise comfort the Children of Moses with the remembrance of this Wronged One. Blessed and happy are they for having turned unto the Divine Countenance, and directed themselves towards the ocean of knowledge in a day whereon all things trembled for fear of God, the All-Glorious, the Most Exalted. Please God, all may be on the Straight Path; may fix their eyes upon His horizon; and may perform that whereunto they have been commanded. We, verily, send at this moment Our salutation unto thee, and unto My servants and My handmaidens from this Glorious and Incomparable Spot.

Concerning the Twin Shining Lights, the Ancient Beauty -- exalted be His glory -- says in the Tablet of the martyred Varqá.

*His exalted Utterance:*

Wealth prevented them not from drawing nigh unto God, and worldly splendour withheld them not from laying down alike their substance and their life. Heavenly Hasan offered up his life as a sacrifice on this nether plane; while Husayn of the domain of mystic meanings lost his life in the most explicit outward sense. What liquor had the one imbibed, and what nectar had the other quaffed? Gracious God! The minds of men are bewildered and astonished. How well did that nomadic desert-dweller say:

Ne'er a hair of my felt raiment * I'd give, were the world my payment.

By "felt raiment" he intended an expression of his love and devotion. Gracious God! Although the afore-mentioned souls were possessed of outward wealth and standing, and of honour and exaltation amidst mankind, yet were the things they possessed incapable of debarring them from the things that are with God.

In the Lawh-i-Kitábu's-Sidq (Tablet of the Book of Truth), He says.

*His exalted Utterance:*

The incident of the Land of Sád was the occasion for heart-consuming grief, and for wailing and lamentation among God's servants. Yet, should a person of discernment think deeply upon the matter, and consider it in a state of absolute detachment from the world of being, he would perceive that there hath never been, nor is there now, any more glorious a matter than that which hath befallen: in so asserting, this servant speaketh as one who is acquainted in detail with the circumstances of the Twin Shining Lights from the beginning even until now. Briefly, they attained in 'Iráq unto the Most Holy Court, where the utmost loving-kindness was shown them. This matter fell out at first contrary to the imaginations of some; howbeit the Hand of Divine power raised them up; arrayed them with the robe of honour; and from the heaven of bounty rained down blessings upon them, until at last they attained the station that thou hast seen, and whereof thou hast heard. After their return from the Most Holy Court unto the Land of Sád, they despatched hither two letters wherein, with utmost lowliness and ardour, they besought of Him Who is the All-Possessing, the Most High, the very thing which actually befell. Consider now: praise be to God, so long as they lived, they were seen to occupy, through the loving-kindness of the One True God, a position of the utmost honour among His servants, love for them indeed having been instilled into people's hearts to a degree that none save God, the True One, hath ever been, or is now, able to reckon; while at the end of their days they attained unto that Supreme Sacrifice which they themselves had sought. Thereafter too thou hast witnessed what was sent down concerning them from the Pen of the Most High. I swear by God! By reason of that which hath been revealed for them all things lament; the Rock (Peter) crieth out; and the inmates of Paradise weep sore. Should anyone possess the whole earth, and bestow it all, never would he attain unto such a station. This is a station for which all the Divine Messengers, and those who have drawn nigh unto God, have ever hoped, and do so still. Till now, well nigh a hundred Tablets have been revealed touching this supreme calamity; nay more, inasmuch as it is observed that in these days too mention is made of the martyrs in some of the Tablets.

In My Name, the Exile, the Sorrowful
