Alas, alas, O thou King of Fidelity! And again alas, alas, O thou Prince of Equity in the realm of creation! Do we see thee a prisoner in the hands of the most wretched among God's creatures; or do we see thee a martyr in the path of God, the Lord of all mankind? I swear by Thy glory, O thou My Name Há'! Grievous is it to the people of Bahá' to hear what hath befallen thee in the love of God, the Lord of the throne on high and of earth below! Grievous is it to the Most Great Name to behold the world, yet to behold thee not; to hear the tumult of the nations, yet to hear neither thy cry nor the voice of thy communion! God is My witness! All things bewail thy tribulation, while the Pen of the Most High weepeth betwixt the fingers of Him Who is the Lord of all Names. We testify that whoever arose to inflict harm upon thee is of those who, throughout all ages, have disbelieved in God, the Lord of this world and of the next. Thou art he through whom the preamble of the Book of Fidelity hath been illuminated in the kingdom of creation, and the Temple of Servitude hath been decked forth among them who are the manifestations of names. Fie upon a people who wronged thee, when through thee the Balance of Justice had been set in the days of thy Lord, the All-Glorious. Thus have We made mention of thee aforetime, and at this moment, with My Most Exalted Pen.

He is the Wronged One

Alas, alas, O God of Mercy! Thou wast wont at all times to comfort those of Thy servants who had been touched by tribulations in Thy days; yet who today will comfort Thee in this trial before which all trials have bowed down, and in this sorrow through which all sorrows have been dumbfounded? I was wont to see Thee, O Thou Wronged One of the World, console Thy chosen ones in adversity and affliction; yet who today will console Thee in this grief through which the face of the earth hath been changed, and all hearts have been consumed? Alas, I cry, with an anguish exceeding that of every ardent sigh, and a fervour whereby the world hath trembled and the hearts of the nations have been consumed, inasmuch as I see Thee plunged into such sorrow that thou delightest not even to hear the name Ridván, how much less to contemplate Thy favours and bounties which have been so plentifully vouchsafed therein. O my Lord, the fire of oppression blazeth throughout the world: where is the light of Thy justice, O Thou Who art the Everlasting King? I swear by Thy might, O Thou Wronged, Imprisoned One! Grievous is it to me to see the Temple of Justice in the clutches of oppression; and grievous is it to me to see the Dawning-place of Fidelity in the hands of the wicked doers. I know not, O my Lord, and the Lord of earth and heaven, whether he hath quaffed from the fount of martyrdom, or bideth still at the mercy of them through whom the ensigns of tyranny were planted amidst mankind. I swear by Thy sovereignty, O Thou the Beloved of creation, and the Desire of all things visible and invisible! Were the eyes of the whole world to weep, and the hearts of all nations to be consumed, it would still be unworthy of this affliction, wherein all things hear the clamour of Thine heart and the lamentation of Thy soul. I bear witness that this is a tribulation such as no pen can describe nor any tongue recount. The matter is in the hand of God, the Lord of creation.

He is the Faithful Announcer

O Land of Sád! Where is he who loved God and His chosen ones, and where is he who was under all conditions occupied in His service? Where is he who shone forth above the horizon of fidelity like unto the sun rising above the earth's horizon? Where is he whom I had entrusted unto thee? Hast thou delivered him into the hands of his enemies, or hath he laid down his life in the path of God, the Lord of all names? Tell Me, what have the people done with him through whom the Cause of God was made manifest among His servants, and the horizon of amity illumined in every land? Tell Me truly, where is the Most Great Trust? And where is he that circled around God, the Lord of the throne on high and of earth below? Where is that spirit who became embodied in human form that he might render service unto God, the Supreme Ordainer? O Land of Sád! Where is the spreading tree of love, its boughs and branches, its leaves and fruits? In answer she crieth out, saying: "I swear by Thy Beauty, O Thou Who art the King of Glory, and the Beloved of Há'! Powerless am I to recount what I have seen perpetrated by the enemies. By Thy might! I shame to tell what the people have done with him who was their lord, their master, their succourer, and their helper. How can I speak of that whereby Thine heart will be saddened, O Thou Who art the Desire of earth and heaven? Every time I purpose to speak, I am prevented by my weeping. Thou indeed art He Who knoweth man's secret thought and private conversation. By Thy might, O Thou Who art my King! Wert Thou to decree mine extinction, more welcome would it be to me than to make mention, and to discourse, before Thee of that which would occasion sorrows during the days which Thou hast appointed as the dawning-places of happiness unto Thy loved ones, and the daysprings of joy unto the dwellers of Thy realm. This I say, confident as I am in the ocean of Thy knowledge, the heaven of Thy Purpose, the pervasive influence of Thy Will, and the all-encompassing scope of Thy might. Would that I had never existed, rather than that I should have seen Thee sorrowful, O Thou Lord of the nations, and King of everlasting days!" O Clime of Sád! Alack, how is it that I see thy herds of camels, and hear their braying, yet see not My she-camel, neither hear her plaintive call? Is she in the meadows above the earth, or doth she lie beneath them? O gardens of that city! Where is the breeze of God that bloweth over thee? And where is the Fruit of God within thee? Hath it been plucked, or hath it fallen? I swear by God! The people, truly, are in grievous error. They have hamstrung the She-Camel, although she had supplied them with purest milk from the breast of the wisdom of God, the Lord of all worlds. O My Name Há'! We, verily, concealed thy station whilst thou wast on earth, by reason of the frailty of Our servants: then, when thou wast ascended, We revealed thee, and made manifest all that thou art, and that which God, the Almighty, the All-Praised, had bestowed upon thee. Blessed is he who loveth thee; who delighteth in communion with thee; who hearkeneth unto thy call, thy remembrance, and thy praise; who directeth his steps towards thy resting-place; and who turneth his face unto thy face in the path of God, thy Beloved, thine Aim, and thy Revealer. Blessed is every visitor who visiteth thy most exalted shrine and thy most glorious seat; who standeth before thy grave, and who addresseth thee in the words that were revealed by the Pen of the Most High, and which the Tongue of Grandeur uttered in the prison-city of 'Akká. Happy is he that remembereth thy days, and all that appeared from thee in the love of God, thy Lord; and who relateth unto the people that which befell thee in the service of the Cause of thy Lord. By God! He, verily, is numbered with the people of Bahá' in a noble Tablet. O My Name Há'! Thou art he who was in his own homeland a stranger, in his dwelling-place a prisoner, and among God's servants oppressed and forsaken. Blessed is the land that God hath made the repository of thy mortal form, and the city above whose horizon thou didst shine forth during the days of thy Lord. It behoveth every lover to make mention of thee in the same words wherewith God hath made mention of thee in His Tablets. And we beseech Him through thee to send down upon His loved ones that which will draw them nigh unto Him; He, verily, is the Forgiving, the Gracious.

He is the Comforter, the Consoler, the Exalted, the Most Glorious

Glory be unto Thee, O Thou Who art the King of names, for that Thou hast converted joy into vexation, and pitched the tent of sorrows during Thy festival of Ridván. I swear by Thy glory! I repine not at that which hath befallen Me in Thy path. By Thy name, O Thou Who art the Lord of all names! Tribulation borne for love of Thee is, verily, My cherished wish, the goal of My desire, and the solace of Mine heart; yet do I long to announce unto the world that from the Lote Tree of Fidelity the Most Exalted Fruit hath fallen, inasmuch as it was compassed by tempestuous winds blowing from the right hand of Thy decree, and smitten by the assault of Thine appointment as inscribed by the Pen of Thy behest. O My Lord! The sea of troubles hath surged during the days of Thy happiness, and the fragrance of sorrows hath wafted even in the day of Thy blissful joy. Hath the refulgent orb of Thy Name Há' set beneath the horizon of Sád, or is he still in the clutches of the enemies, who have cast away Thy Testament, O Thou Who art the Possessor of all names? O Land of Sád! Doth My Name yet walk upon thy surface, or hath there reposed within thy womb a trust from Me? O insensate land! How canst thou be still, when the very ocean is concealed within thee? And how canst thou be illumined, when the refulgent orb hath set beneath thy horizon? O Land of Sád! Where is thy lamp, and where thy straight path? Where is God's overflowing fount within thee, and where the Lote Tree whose shade God had made a shelter unto all that resorted thither, or sought it out, or chanced upon it in their travels? I swear by God! O My Name Há'! By reason of thine agony the Pen of the Most High hath halted; the dwellers of the Cities of the Names of God have lamented; and the hearts of His chosen ones have melted. Thou art he who accepted not a ransom in the love of God, the Lord of this world and of the next; and repeatedly craved of God that which actually befell him. Thou art the Most Great Ransom in the Crimson Book. Did the people think that they had gained by their transaction? Nay, by Him Who is the King of Names! God is My witness that they suffered a loss such as hath had no equal in the knowledge of God, the Lord of the throne above and of earth below. The Tongue of Grandeur testifieth that it is thou who hast gained by this transaction. Nay by My life! All gain is thine, inasmuch as thou hast quit the earth, whose every atom beareth witness unto its evanescence; hast set thy face towards the dawning-place of eternity; and hast yielded thy life in thy yearning for the love of God, the Creator of the heavens and the Lord of all names. By thy life, O My Name! By reason of thine agony the afflictions of the saints have been effaced, and the eyes of God's chosen ones and the Celestial Concourse have run down with tears. It hath reached such a pass that He Who is the Manifestation of God's Ancient Beauty among the nations hath been sorrowed. Wert thou present before this Wronged One in thine outward temple, and didst behold in what condition the Pen of the Most High recounteth thine afflictions, thou wouldst wail even as a bereaved mother in the kingdom of creation. Alas, alas, O My Name Há'! And again alas, alas, O My Name that shineth above the horizon of fidelity! And yet again, alas I cry, with a fervour such as to cause oceans to well forth from the eyes, and the hearts and souls to melt. Thou art he through whom the tale of the Sacrifice (Ishmael) hath been retold, and that which had been hidden in the knowledge of God, and written in His Mighty Book, hath come to pass. O Land of Sád! Speak true, I prithee, and tell Me, Where is the She-Camel of God, that trod thy byways and grazed in thy fair pastures? Doth she still graze today, or hath she been hamstrung by the enemies of God, and by the enemies of His chosen ones and His servants? Then tell Me, did she drink and ascend, or did she suffer martyrdom whilst parched, and so ascend unto the Abhá Horizon and the realms above? Then tell Me, left she anyone behind to guard her home; to gather together her kin; to calm their trepidation; to fortify their hearts; to comfort them in their distress; and to console them in their grief and sorrow? Thou must needs in such a case, and at this very moment, repeat: The Kingdom is God's the Lord of the worlds! Verily, we are God's, and unto Him shall we indeed return.

He is the Rememberer, the All-Knowing

Glory be unto Thee, O Lord My God! Thou seest and knowest what hath befallen Thy chosen ones during the days of Thy Revelation, and dost behold and witness the things they have borne for love of Thee and for the sake of Thy pleasure. O My Lord! The chronicles of the world attest the abasement of Thy loved ones and the glory of Thine enemies, while the books of all peoples bear witness unto the powerlessness of Thy chosen ones and the might of those who disbelieved in Thy signs. Thou hearest, O My God, at this moment, the sighs, the prayers, the invocations, and the intercessions I utter on behalf of such of Thy creatures as are nigh unto Thee, and such of Thy people as have recognized Thy oneness. Thy glory beareth Me witness, O Thou Who art the Sovereign of the realm above, and the Ruler of the kingdom! I know of a surety that abasement in Thy path is an honour with which no worldly honour can compare, and that even fire in Thy love is a light such as the veils of all peoples cannot obscure. Were I to quaff, O My God, at every moment the cup of tribulation from the hands of Mine enemies, never would the thirst of My yearning and the drought of My longing be quenched. He that hath once quaffed the pure beverage of Thy love, and been inebriated by the wine of Thy knowledge, shall never be downcast by aught that is in Thine earth, nor distracted by any matter from fixing his eyes upon the horizon of Thy Revelation, and upon Thy most effulgent Beauty and Thy most sublime and lofty station. My Most Exalted Pen, verily, longeth that its own shrill voice, its piteous cry and plaintive clamour should at all times be raised in this affliction, which hath caused the denizens of Paradise and the dwellers of the All-Highest Heaven to lament. It hath come to such a pass that the Tongue of Him Who is the Revealer of Thy Cause, the Ocean of Thy knowledge, and the Dayspring of Thine inspiration is occupied with mourning, in token of His grace, His mercy, and His fidelity. O My Name Há'! Thou, verily, art in the Most Exalted Paradise, and thine head hath been adorned with the crown of the loving-kindness of thy Lord, the Possessor of all names; while those that love thee are in such a state of despondency that the clouds weep for them in the daytime and in the night season. Dost thou now reveal the true aspect of thy station, or dost thou yet conceal it, even as thy Lord was wont to conceal it as a precaution on His part? Thy Lord, truly, is the All-Wise, the All-Knowing. Thou art he through whom the Most Great Sacrifice hath been made manifest, and its reality established among the nations. O My Name Há'! I swear by God that through thee the horizon of fidelity hath been illumined, and that which hath resulted in the diffusion of the Cause of God, the Creator of the heavens, hath been revealed. Blessed is the eye that weepeth for thy sufferings; the ear that hearkeneth unto thy praise; the face that turneth towards thee; and the soul that hasteneth to attain thy resting-place, the spot that hath been honoured to receive thy noble earthly frame and thy sanctified and precious temple. By God! The hearts have been consumed by reason of the calamity that befell thee, and the vitals lacerated by reason of thy tragic fate. O Land of Sád! I adjure thee by the Well-Beloved, to tell Me, hath the fragrance of the lover, through whom the perfume of the Divine raiment was wafted among the people of sanctity, ceased to pervade thee? And is he fallen into the clutches of every oppressor that hath disbelieved in God and His Verses, and hath turned away from His Countenance and His sovereignty? O gentle gale! Hast thou come from the quarter of the lover unto the Well-Beloved with tidings such as to rejoice the souls, or with an annunciation fit to sear the hearts? O thou breath of My native land! By My life! I inhale not from thee the fragrance of him that loved Me. 'Tis like he hath winged his flight from this earth's bough unto the realms above and the Abhá Horizon. O My Name! Blessed the eye that weepeth over thy sufferings, whereat My Name Há' in the Land of Taff (Karbilá) crieth aloud and saith: "O thou Name Há'! By thy life! Through thy suffering mine own sufferings, my sorrows, mine anguish and mine affliction have been renewed." O Earth of the City! Relate thou what betided him and his brother when they attended the gathering of the oppressors, who had at no time inhaled the sweet savour of equity, and who chose rather the part of arbitrariness. By God! Through them the Word of God which proceeded out of the mouth of the Primal Will was established upon the throne of revelation. He said, and truly did He speak: "Verily, I and all who are in Paradise in pursuance of the Most Great Justice do yearn to meet a soul that hath been slain in His path." Thus spake He in truth, and that which had been concealed in the knowledge of God was made manifest. My Tongue testifieth in the Kingdom of Mine Utterance that the twain were martyred in My path, and that My heart and My pen, and those that have circled around My throne, soared in the heaven of My nearness, and quaffed the choice wine of My favours from the hands of My loving-kindness, have bewailed them. O My Name, and My loved ones! Although the calamity that befell you is such that the Concourse on High and the inmates of the all-glorious Tabernacle have wailed and lamented, yet doth this Wronged One give praise unto God, and yield Him thanks, inasmuch as He graciously assisted you to recognize the Dawning-place of His Cause, and so elevated your stations that His Most Exalted Pen mourneth over you in this most sublime station. Blessed is the soul that turneth towards you; the heart that attaineth unto your love; the visitor that visiteth your resting-place; and the seeker that entereth into your land, cleaveth unto your cord, and payeth homage to your shrine. By the righteousness of God! These, truly, are of the blissful; and these, truly, are numbered among His favoured servants in the Book of God, the King, the Inaccessible, the Most Great. Praise be to God, the Lord of all that was and shall be. Verily, we are God's, and unto Him shall we return.

In My Name, the All-Glorious, the Most Bountiful

O Land of Sád! Where is the Most Great Sacrifice, he that accepted not a ransom in the path of God, the Lord of all mankind? And where are they that were martyred by reason of their love for this Youth, Who no sooner did He appear than the backs of the idols that had pronounced judgment against the Bearers of the Trust of God, the Lord of the worlds, were broken? O branch of My Lote Tree! Where is My dove that would ever pour forth its songs, its joyful warblings and gentle cooings? Hath it winged its flight unto the realms above, or have the wrong-doers seized it with the talons of hatred betwixt earth and heaven? I prithee inform Me, and be not of the reticent! Where are the brilliant stars, the shining orbs, the signal months, the lustrous days, and the effulgent lights? By God, they have set, disappeared, been veiled from sight, and returned whence they had come; yet are the people in patent discord. O My Ridván! How is it that I see thy birds, and hear their songs, yet see not My dove, neither hear its melodies? Remaineth it yet in this vain life, or hath it winged its flight unto the Eternal Garden? Recount to Me its tale, nor be of them that hold their peace! "O great and omnipotent Master! Long have Thy sorrows lasted, wherefore the hearts of Thy chosen ones are bewildered, and the dwellers in Thy Tabernacle have bewailed Thee. I swear by Thy glory! Thy call and Thy commemoration have not ceased. I hear each dawn Thy sighs; each day Thy groaning; and each night Thy plaints and piteous cries. Have pity on Thy servants and Thy loved ones! I bear witness, O Thou My Best-Beloved, that to suffer martyrdom in Thy path hath ever been the hope of Thy Prophets and the Bearers of Thy Trust." So indeed affirmed the Point of the Bayán, Who suffered martyrdom in Thy path; He said, and truly did He speak: "O Thou Remnant of God! I have sacrificed Myself wholly for Thee; I have accepted curses for Thy sake, and have yearned for naught but martyrdom in the path of Thy love." Whoso attaineth unto this most sublime station hath attained unto all good both in this world and in the next. Thou art He Who testifieth in truth, and Thou, verily, art the All-Knowing, the All-Informed.

O Thou Lord of Utterance!

Peace, hold thy tongue! Thou hast o'erstepped thy bound! Return thou unto God, and be of the penitent. Wouldst thou question any act of Him Who it behoveth not should be asked of His doings? Take thou refuge with God, Who created thee and fashioned thee, and be not of the heedless. Thou hast not attained so much as the shore of one of the oceans of the wisdom of thy Lord, how much less their boundless floods and fathomless deeps, and whatsoever hath been hidden in His knowledge, which transcendeth all worlds. He it is through Whom the ensign of "He doeth whatsoever He willeth" hath been planted, and the standard of "He shall not be asked of that which He hath wrought" hath been hoisted upon every lofty peak. O Wayfarer of the Spirit! Renounce this theme, and all that is uttered in the kingdom of creation; then set thyself to attain the far-off goal and the most august seat, the station which hath been adorned with the lights of the supernal realm, and been honoured by the glances of the loving-kindness of God, the Sovereign of the kingdoms of earth and heaven. We, verily, have purposed that thou shouldst be the first wayfarer and the first visitor to convey on the part of Him Who is the Dawning-place of Sanctity the sweet fragrance of the Divine raiment unto a land wherein have appeared the Supreme Sacrifice and they who were the Most Great Ransoms. We counsel thee to be on thy guard, for the Wolf howleth and the She-Serpent hisseth.

*When thou hast drawn nigh unto the city, and perceived its traces, halt thou and say:*

O City of the Lover! Where is the ocean of the love of God, and where the ships that sailed upon it? Where are thy flowing springs, and where thy brilliant stars, breaking forth above the horizon? Where are thy lofty and refulgent diadems, and where thy shining and resplendent moons? Prithee tell what have the oppressors done with them: is it such as may flow forth from the pen, or such as all pens would be powerless to recount? The matter is in the hand of God, the Lord of all men. O City of the Lover! By the righteousness of God! That which they bore at the hands of the oppressors shall not have been in vain. Unto this beareth witness He Who hath knowledge of all things, whether secret or open, and Who mourneth His loved ones and His chosen ones in token of His grace, His fidelity, His loving-kindness and His favours. By Him Who is the Truth! They, verily, have secured a mighty gain, although the people are in evident doubt.

*Set then thyself towards the Holy Martyrs' Tombs and the Exalted Shrines,* *and, when thou hast known, hast found, and come before them, stand and say:*

The first light that shone forth from the horizon of the revelation of the Face of your Lord, the Creator of the Heavens, be upon you, O ye the manifestations of fidelity, and the dawning-places of names in the kingdom of creation! I testify that through you the standards of victory have been manifested, the ensigns of guidance have been hoisted, the horizon of steadfastness hath been illumined, and the breeze of God hath been wafted amidst mankind; and through you the glory of sacrifice hath been renewed, and that which hath caused the hearts and minds to marvel hath appeared. It is ye who sacrificed all that ye possessed, your spirits, your every limb and vein, in the path of God, your Well-Beloved and your hearts' Desire. It is ye whom neither the wrong of the oppressor, nor the blame of the blamer, nor the onslaught of every disbeliever who turned away from God when he came invested with a sovereignty that hath encompassed all who are in heaven and on earth, could deter from following in His way. I testify that the Celestial Concourse, and with them the dwellers of the All-Glorious Tabernacle, have bewailed your agony; while on behalf of every believer the Tongue of God, the Help in Peril, the Self-Subsisting, hath spoken: "Verily, we are God's, and unto Him shall we return." In all conditions, praise be to God, the Lord of all that was and shall be.

*Then beseech of God whatsoever thou desirest of His bounty; He, verily, is the All-Glorious, the All-Loving.*

He is the Most Holy, the Most Great

O thou companion! I swear by God! The tale of the Sacrifice (Ishmael), and that which was hidden in the knowledge of God, the Lord of the worlds, hath been repeated. The bird of fidelity hath winged its flight from this earth's bough unto the Sadratu'l-Muntahá, by reason of that which the hands of the oppressors have wrought. We testify that he is now wrapt in an ecstasy of joy such as no mortal joy can rival, while his lovers are so immersed in sorrow that all things weep for them. Thy Lord, truly, is the All-Bountiful, the All-Knowing. God is My witness! It was they, verily, who gained by this transaction, and the wrong-doers who lost. These, of a surety, are in grievous loss. Was it Husayn who lost by laying down his life in the path of God, or was it those that wronged him, through having followed every impious miscreant, far gone in error? Oppression hath reached such a pitch that the tongue, and beyond it every knowledgeable assayer, are powerless to describe it. They have lit a fire whose blaze shall not be extinguished in the world. Thus informeth thee He with Whom is the knowledge of all things, as recorded in a Lucid Book. O Khalíl! Observe thou to what degree the rightness of the truth and the waywardness of falsehood have become clear and evident! All bear witness that the utmost affection, mercy and loving-kindness were shown by that wronged one towards all peoples, while no untoward action, such as might become a cause of mischief or an occasion of disorder, ever emanated from him. How many the poor of foreign nations whom he succoured during the days of hardship. Unto this testify all who speak truly, and beyond them thy Lord, the All-Informed. Should anyone reflect upon him, and the marks of loving-kindness shown him by his Lord, he would see with the eye of certitude that in what hath befallen there was, and is, a surpassing wisdom. The Supreme Ransom and the Most Great Sacrifice have been made manifest in this Mighty Cause. In 'Iráq, when he entered the Most Holy Court, the utmost loving-kindness was shown him by the Source of Command, to the degree that certain souls spoke in a manner that revealed them to be wandering in the wilds of fancy. Thereafter, with consummate power, the One True God raised up that lote tree to a station whereof none but Him, the All-Knowing, is apprised; and sent down for him a blessing from His presence and a mercy from His side. He, verily, is the Almighty, the Most Powerful. Divers letters arrived from him before the throne, wherein he besought his Lord, the Possessor of this world and of the next, to ordain that he might attain unto the Supreme Sacrifice. By thy life, O Khalíl! By reason of that which befell him, all other calamities have been effaced. Unto this testifieth thy Lord, the Wronged One, the Exile. We have sent down from the heaven of grace that wherewith the kingdoms of earth and heaven can never be compared: erelong shall God cause that which hath been planted in the land of utterance to germinate; He, verily, is the All-Powerful, Whom the hosts of the world and the cohorts of the oppressors are powerless to frustrate. O Khalíl! From time immemorial even until now, the Divine Lote Tree, which the hand of God's sovereign purpose hath planted in the good and blessed land, hath been watered by the blood of them that are wholly devoted to His Cause, and truly recognize His unity. Soon, through the acts of the oppressors, shall it stand revealed and manifest in the land. Hath the oppressor imagined that God is heedless of that which he hath wrought? Nay, by Him Who is potent over all things! I swear by the Sovereign Truth! God shall make outwardly manifest in the land whatsoever He hath sent down in the Book: unto this testify all who discern the truth in things, through the guidance of God, the Lord of the worlds. Consider the Súriy-i-Ra'ís and other Tablets. By the righteousness of God! Thine heart, and the hearts of all who are endued with understanding, shall be rejoiced by that which hath been revealed therein. Verily, should He wish it, He could lay hold on all the peoples of the earth through a word from Him; howbeit He revealeth His Cause pursuant to a wisdom that lieth hidden in his all-embracing knowledge. I swear by the Sun of Might! Had the world been possessed of any value, never would the Ancient Beauty have consented to tarry for so many years in the Most Great Prison. So long as man abideth on earth, he remaineth, now as formerly, in a state of stupefaction; excepting only those whose hearts are empty of attachment, and who look into things with the eye of God. Please God, thou wilt, so far as thou art able, impart tranquillity and assurance unto illumined hearts, that they may be filled with tranquillity after perturbation, and with gladness after sorrow. Thus commandeth thee He Who remembereth thee in this glorious station. O Khalíl! A mighty happening hath come to pass in the world. Though yet greater hath previously occurred, even as thou thyself dost witness and attest, yet, since a considerable period had elapsed during which the Hand of Divine Power had been exercising its protective sway -- when of a sudden this inexorable Divine judgment befell -- for this reason did it become a cause of wailing, of weeping and of great commotion. Yet hath thy Lord in store that whereby the hearts shall be rejoiced after this mighty sorrow. Say: This is a sacrifice whose effects have penetrated the world. Erelong shall God make them manifest through the power of truth; potent is He to do whatsoever He willeth. The Glory of God rest upon thee, and upon all them that have hearkened unto thy word in the Cause of God, the Lord of the Day of Reckoning.

He is the One that Speaketh before the Divine Countenance

O ye dwellers of the cities and villages! Hearken ye unto that which the Tongue proclaimeth in the kingdom of utterance on the part of Him Who hath caused all things to proclaim: "There is none other God but Me, the Incomparable, the All-Knowing!" He it is Who hath sent down the Books, and sent forth the Messengers, announcing through them: "There is none other God but Me, the Ever-Watchful, the All-Wise!" All things have been privileged to hearken unto the Call, save every unconscionable transgressor; and every eye hath beheld God's All-Glorious Horizon, save every heedless one that is far astray. By God! The Most Sublime Vision hath been made manifest, and He Who is the Supreme Ordainer calleth aloud and saith: "Members of the human race! The Great Day hath come; the Moon hath been cleft in twain; and all are caught up in a wondrous resurrection. That which had lain hidden hath been revealed; that which had been stored away hath been brought forth; and the Promised One hath come down from the heaven of God's decree swifter than the twinkling of an eye. Yet are the people under a plain delusion. They see the sun, yet say, 'Is it indeed a sun?;' and they behold the Verses, yet say, 'Naught are they but a mighty sorcery!' Even so hath it been decreed in the Book; yet are the people that are wrapped in veils assailed by strange misgivings!" O ye beloved of the All-Merciful throughout the world! This Wronged One, verily, adjureth you by the Beloved of creation, Who speaketh forth in the kingdom of utterance, that ye deal not faithlessly with the property of others. Be ye the trustees of God in His cities, and the daysprings of truthfulness in His lands. Blessed is he that hearkeneth unto the counsel of God, and is of those who put it into effect. Such instances of faithlessness have been encountered in this exile that Mine heart hath melted, Mine eye hath wept, My soul hath lamented, and My breast hath been sore straitened. By the righteousness of God! Sleep hath fled from the eyes of Bahá' by reason of that which hath befallen Him in this snow-white Spot. To this all things testify; yet are the people sunk in heedlessness. The Rock (Peter) hath cried out by reason of the trials I have suffered, and the Divine Lote Tree hath lamented on account of the hardships I have endured. God is My witness! I sorrow not for Myself, but for the Cause of God, the Lord of the worlds. All sorrows are His Who is precluded from making mention of the trials and hardships that have touched Him in this noble habitation! We hearken unto falsehood and observe silence, and the speaker conceiveth that he hath imposed upon Us, and that We have found his words to be conspicuously true. O My loved ones! Array yourselves in the Divine virtues, and adorn your temples with the robes of trustworthiness, of steadfastness and of truthfulness; thus hath the Lord of creation commanded you in the Guarded Tablet. Our sorrows have lately been compounded, inasmuch as We behold the temple of love, and those that are with him, caught in the clutches of malice at the hands of the hosts of their oppressors. Say ye: "O Thou Who art the Lord of all Names, and the Creator of the heavens! We ask Thee by this martyr, who hath yielded his life in these days so that he may proclaim Thy Cause and exalt Thy Word, to send down upon Thy loved ones and Thy chosen ones that which shall preserve them from the clutches of heedlessness and doubt. Give them, then, to drink, from the hands of Thy bounteousness, the living waters of certitude. Thou, verily, art the Bestower, the Beneficent. No God is there but Thee, the Gracious, the Giver, the Generous."

He is the Rememberer, the Sorrowful

O Land of Sád! Relate thou what the people have done with the family of the Prophet, and what hath befallen the children of the Virgin at the hands of thy dwellers. O Land of Sád! The Sun of the Hijáz inquireth of thee after His family, and the spotless Virgin after her sons and her daughter. Have the oppressors entombed them in a darksome well, or have they drawn them forth with the cords of malice in order to subject them to a fresh affliction? By the life of the Beloved! The powers of heaven have been shaken by this dire calamity. Alas, alas! The Luminary of Bathá (Mecca) hath lamented amongst the Celestial Concourse by reason of that which hath befallen His family at the hands of them who are the embodiments of malice. O dwellers of Sád! Ye have committed that whereat those who are the very dawning-places of presumption and the daysprings of rebellion in this world are astounded. Judge ye fairly: By what proof did ye slay them through whom the Cause of the All-Merciful hath been diffused throughout the East and the West? Alas, alas! Through you the Ark of the Prophet hath been broken, and the offspring of the Virgin have been drowned; and through you happiness hath been converted into sorrows, and darkness hath overtaken all peoples, save only those whom the All-Merciful hath pleased to spare. O dwellers of Sád! Hearken ye unto the words wherewith Muhammad, the Apostle of God, calleth you from the Supreme Horizon: "O ye perverse and wicked generation! Where is My Hasan, who was ablaze with the fire of the love of God in the kingdom of creation, and adorned with the ornament of fidelity betwixt earth and heaven? And where is My Husayn, who accepted not a ransom in the path of God, the Lord of all mankind? By My life! O ye company of evil-doers! No room hath been left you to excuse or justify yourselves, in virtue of My words: 'The pious are God's and the impious are Mine.' Do ye conceive yourselves believers, and do ye account yourselves among the people of the Furqán? Nay, by Him Who is the All-Merciful! Whosoever among the learned is clothed in the raiment of virtue hath deplored your deed; and whosoever among the wise is adorned with the ornament of justice hath exclaimed in protest at your actions. The voice of the lamentation of the Celestial Concourse hath been raised on account of your oppression, and all things have cried out by reason of that which your hands have wrought. Ye read the Qur'án, yet repudiate its Root, and Him that sent it down; and ye acknowledge My prophetic mission, yet slay My children, and turn away from Him that sent Me forth. I am bewildered at you, O ye concourse of the hateful! Yea, all that hath been created by the Word of God, the Help in Peril, the Self-Subsisting, is similarly perplexed." O Wayfarer of the deep! Where are Thy ships? Have they broken upon the rocks of disbelief and discord, or have they foundered under the battering winds of oppression and malice? Have they journeyed from the cities of the bodies unto the gardens of the souls, or have they migrated from the wilderness of separation and remoteness unto the station of nearness, sanctity and reunion? "O Prince of the world! Thy might and Thy sovereignty bear Me witness! Powerless am I to relate how the winds of oppression have assailed them. I swear by Thine own Self! It shameth Me to disclose that which I have seen and known. Thou indeed knowest best what is in Me, yet know I not what is in Thee. Thou, truly, art the All-Knowing, the All-Wise. Howbeit this word shall I speak in token of My submission unto Thine irresistible command, and Mine observance of Thine incontrovertible decree: The nightingale hath taken flight, inasmuch as the croaking of the raven hath been raised. The command belongeth to God, the Incomparable, the All-Knowing."

I am the Wronged One, the Exile

O Samandar! By thy life! The affliction of Muhammad, the Apostle of God, hath been renewed in the All-highest Paradise, and thereto the anguish of the spotless Virgin in the Most Exalted Station. "Fie upon you, O people of the Furqán!" she exclaimeth, "Ye have wrought even that which ye wrought aforetime! Where is my Hasan, and where my Husayn? Announce their fate, nor be of them that turn away! Did my Hasan deal faithlessly amongst you, unlawfully devour your wealth, or shed your blood? Judge ye fairly, O people, and be not of them that speak falsely! Explain ye, O people of the Furqán! For what crime did ye slay my Husayn in the Land of Sád?" By My life, O thou who hast fixed thy gaze upon My Countenance! The Ark hath been shattered, and the She-Camel hath been hamstrung by reason of that which the hands of the oppressors have wrought. The Tale of Taff (Karbilá) hath been retold; yet are the people wrapped in a palpable veil. We, verily, concealed the station of My Name Hasan by reason of the frailty of Our servants; then, when he was ascended on the wings of the spirit unto the realms above, We disclosed a part of that which God had bestowed upon him, in token of His grace: He, verily, is the Most Gracious, the All-Bountiful. Know further: That which hath come to pass shall exert an influence in the world: erelong shall this become apparent through the sovereignty of God, the Almighty, the Most Powerful. Oppression hath reached the pitch that alike the pen and the tongue are powerless and inadequate to recount or express it. Souls who at no time harmed another soul; who comported themselves with perfect love and kindliness; and who lived on terms of friendliness with all the peoples and kindreds of the earth -- behold what was inflicted upon them! Were it to be inquired of those two embodiments of ignorance who regard themselves as learned, "Wherefore slew ye these wronged ones, notwithstanding that no crime or sin had been committed on their part?," they would, in reply, undoubtedly repeat the same words uttered by the mouths of the infidels in respect of the Prince of Martyrs -- may all else but him be His sacrifice. After the business of the Land of Káf, the company of the oppressors were wont to repeat this utterance:

"Husayn beyond his limit stray'd, * so slain was, by his grandsire's blade."

Fie upon them, and upon those that have followed in their footsteps! This apart, what blame attached unto the Prophet's children who were in that household? This business shall never be obliterated from the tablet of creation. For all four souls there hath been sent down from the heaven of God's loving-kindness that which hath changed the world's happiness into grief. Although to outward seeming the people of oppression are complacent about the deed they have committed, yet, by My life, their realities curse them, and lament over them, albeit they neither hear, nor feel, nor know it. Do thou convey Our salutation unto all the friends. Please God, all may, with the utmost joy and radiance, be occupied with the remembrance of God, and lay hold upon, and cleave tenaciously unto, the strong cord of patience and fortitude. Cast thou, on My behalf, a salutation over thy brother's countenance. We ask Him, exalted be He, graciously to confirm him, and to ordain for him that which shall profit him. He, verily, is the All-Knowing, the All-Wise. We seal Our utterance with the mention of God, the Help in Peril, the Self-Subsisting: "Verily, we are God's, and unto Him shall we return."

In My Name, the One Sanctified above the World of Being

The Book of Generosity, sent down by the King of everlasting days! Whoever adorneth himself therewith is of those that are celebrated amongst men, and whom the All-Merciful blesseth from His inaccessible and glorious realm. Yet for all the excellence of its worth and the grandeur of its station, if it exceed its due bounds it is designated "extravagance" by Him Who is the All-Knowing, the All-Wise. Choose ye the part of moderation: this is that whereunto the All-Possessing, the Most High, hath commanded you in a noble Book. Spend ye, O ye who are the manifestations of this Name and the dawning-places of this Attribute, upon them whom ye find to be in conspicuous poverty. Say: Beware, O possessors of riches, lest the term "conspicuous" hold you back from spending in the path of God, the Lord of the worlds. Say: By the life of God! None is despised in the eyes of his Lord on account of poverty; nay rather doth he increase in stature if He find him to be of them that endure with patience. Blessed the poor one who exerciseth patience; and woe unto the rich one who holdeth back the rights of God, the which have been enjoined upon him in His Guarded Tablet. Say: Pride not yourselves upon your material possessions: reflect upon your final objective, and that which hath been destined as the reward of your actions in the Book of God, the Most Exalted, the Most Great. Blessed the rich one whom riches have not held back from God, the Lord of all names: he, verily, is among the choicest of creatures in the sight of the True One, the Almighty, the All-Knowing. Say: The Great Day hath come, and this, truly, is the springtime of deeds, could ye but know it. Strive ye, O people, that from you may appear that which shall profit you in the worlds of your Lord, the Almighty, the All-Praised. Say: Lay hold upon a praiseworthy character and goodly deeds, and be not of them that tarry. It behoveth every soul to cleave unto that whereby the Cause of God, your Lord, the Most Powerful, the Almighty, may be exalted. Say: Behold ye not this world, its vicissitudes, its variable hues, its changing aspects? How then can ye be content with it, and with aught that it containeth? Open your eyes, and be of them that gaze with discernment. It shall take them off with the speed of lightning; nay faster: to this testifieth the Lord of the kingdom in this wondrous Tablet. Shouldst thou be transported by the rapture born of the Divine Verses, render thanks, and say: "Unto Thee be praise, O Thou the Desire of all them that have sought Thee!" Rejoice thou, inasmuch as the Pen of the Most High hath turned towards thee, and sent down for thee that which the tongues of creation, nay every tongue of matchless eloquence, would be powerless befittingly to extol. Do thou greet on My behalf My loved ones, and gladden them by My remembrance of them; then read out to them My beauteous Tablet. The Glory of God rest upon thee and upon thy family, and whosoever is with thee upon My Straight Path.

He is the Conferrer of Honour

O members of the Household! There hath befallen you in the path of God that which befell the sons of the Apostle, their daughters and their womenfolk, in the Land of Taff (Karbilá) and other lands. Rest ye assured in the grace of God, and in His mercy: He, verily, is with you in every world of His worlds. He, verily, is the Beholder, the Ever-Present, the All-Seeing. Fie upon a people who wronged you, slew you, and pillaged your possessions. By My life! The people are indeed in grievous loss. The blasts of chastisement shall assail them from all sides: He, verily, is the All-Knowing, the All-Informed. Put your trust in God, and say: "Fortunate and blessed are we for that which hath befallen us in His Straight Path. Praise be to God, the Lord of the worlds."

He is the Comforter in this Great and Mighty Station

O Samandar! He Who is the Supreme Ordainer doth, of a truth, comfort His own Self in that which hath befallen Him at the hands of those who chose the part of arbitrariness, and cast equity behind their backs, in consequence of having followed every rebellious demon. 'Ád and Thamúd have, verily, inflicted upon Sálih and Húd that whereat the Sadratu'l-Muntahá hath lamented, and the Concourse on high have cried out: thereto testifieth this Victim of oppression, who is beset by sorrow, and a stranger in a foreign land. I swear by God! They have crucified the Spirit (Jesus); hamstrung the She-Camel; and broken the Ark of the Covenant: thy Lord, verily, is the Expounder, the All-Informed. He, verily, mourneth His chosen ones, and comforteth His loved ones, in this calamity whereat Justice hath lamented, and the Faithful Spirit hath cried out. They have slain My chosen ones, and pillaged their possessions: thus hath it been decreed; yet the people are for the most part unaware. O Samandar! We have seen the beloved Joseph captive between the wolf's fangs, and Husayn caught in the clutches of the oppressors. By the righteousness of God! The people have committed that which neither the Jews inflicted upon the Spirit (Jesus), nor Abú-Jahl upon Muhammad Mine Apostle, Whom We adorned with the ornament of the Seal, and sent forth unto all who are in heaven and on earth. They have wrought that which none in the world hath ever wrought: unto this testifieth He Who is the Ancient King from the seat of this Majestic Vision. After Hasan and Husayn had attained their goal, and the allotted days had passed, We laid hold upon him that was the source of tyranny and injustice, through the power of Our sovereign might. Thy Lord, verily, is the Almighty, the Most Powerful. Blessed are they who draw nigh unto them, and visit them where they lie buried: these, truly, are the people of Bahá' in the kingdom of creation: thus hath it been decreed by the Pen of the Most High in this mighty and wondrous Book. Fie upon those who cast the Tablet of God behind their backs, and followed every wayward miscreant! Reflect thou, O Samandar, upon the patience I exercise notwithstanding My might; the forbearance I evince notwithstanding My power; and the silence I preserve notwithstanding the penetrative influence of My Word, which transcendeth all the worlds. Were it Our wish, We could lay hold on the oppressors in the most explicit outward sense, through the agency of one of our servants, or a company of God's favoured angels. We, verily, act in accordance with the dictates of that same wisdom which We have appointed as a lamp unto My creatures and the dwellers of My realm; thy Lord, truly, is the All-Knowing, the All-Wise. Erelong shall We lay hold upon the workers of oppression, even as We laid hold upon them in the past. Thy Lord, verily, ordaineth what He pleaseth. God grant that thou mayest continue, as heretofore, to be graced by the tokens of God's loving-kindness, and to be occupied with His service. He, verily, testifieth on thy behalf that thou hast been faithful unto His Testament, and remained steadfast in the service of His Cause. Blessed art thou, and thy brother, and thy father who hath ascended unto God, the Lord of the worlds. O Samandar! Thou must needs proceed with the utmost caution. Credit not every speaker, neither reveal that which ye possess unto every stranger, nor disclose it unto every seeker. How many a man professeth with his tongue that whereof no thought hath entered his heart! Be thou stablished upon the throne of wisdom; walk thou in the way of wisdom; and cleave thou unto the cord of wisdom: thus biddeth thee the Lord of all creation; He, verily, is the Faithful Counsellor. In these days some, for the sake of gaining information, or for other purposes, make profession of their devotion and belief. Thou must be in all respects vigilant that naught take place outside the bounds of wisdom. For each of the souls mentioned in thy letter, wondrous and incomparable Verses have been sent down from the heaven of the Will of God. Blessed are they, for that they have been favoured with My Verses during My days, and with My mercy that hath compassed the world. Do thou make mention of thy paternal uncle on My behalf. Say thou: "Grieve not at that which hath befallen thee. The Beloved doth, verily, make mention of thee, and hath turned towards thee as a bounty on His part. He, verily, is the All-Powerful, the All-Bounteous. O Muhammad before Rahím! Blessed art thou, inasmuch as thou hast set thy face towards God; hast hearkened unto His Call; and hast turned unto Him with a heart that is turned unto the Qiblih of the world. Beware lest the vicissitudes of the world sadden thee. The Ocean of Joy, verily, remembereth thee whilst compassed about by sorrows on every hand. The standard of oppression hath been hoisted in the Land of Sád, whereat the Tree of existence hath lamented, and the Rock of the world of being hath cried out. God hath laid hold upon the root of injustice through the power of His sovereign might. He, verily, is the Almighty, the Unrestrained. Say: 'Unto Thee be praise, O my God, for that thou hast made mention of me in Thy Most Great Prison. I ask Thee by Thy Name which overshadoweth the whole world, to write down for me by the Pen of Thy decree that which shall profit me in every world of Thy worlds. O my Lord! Thou knowest what is in me, but I know not that which is with Thee. Thou, verily, art the All-Knowing, the All-Wise.'" Now make We mention of him that hath been named Ibráhím, that he may hearken unto the Call of the All-Glorious, which hath been raised from this Exalted Spot. Do thou at all times make mention of Me, cry out in My Name, and tell forth My beauteous praise. Render thanks unto God for having aided thee to recognize the Truth, and for having sent down for thee that which shall profit thee for so long as the kingdoms of earth and heaven shall endure: provided that thou stand unwaveringly firm in this Cause, through which the feet of the learned have slipped, and the hearts of the wise have trembled, save those whom God, thy Lord and the Lord of all the worlds, hath pleased to spare. Thus hath He Who is the Dawning-place of Revelation made mention of thee during His days, that thou mayest yield thanks unto thy Most Generous Lord. Now make We mention of him that hath been named 'Alí, in this Book wherefrom the fragrance of God's holy utterance hath been diffused throughout the entire creation, and the perfume of the Divine raiment hath been wafted amongst all that are nigh unto Him. O 'Alí! We counsel thee to remain steadfast in this Mighty Cause. How many a man hath laid claim to steadfastness within himself; and who, when We assayed him through a word, faltered, and was of the lost. Abandon thou mere fancy, in the name of thy Lord, the Almighty, the All-Knowing, and lay hold upon the hem of certitude on the part of God, the Inaccessible, the Most Great. In such wise hath the Spirit spoken, the Bird of the Throne warbled, and the Nightingale poured forth its song. Blessed is he who inclineth, and hearkeneth, thereunto; and woe betide the heedless! The Glory of God rest upon thee, and upon all who cleave unto the Cord of God, the Lord of the Day of Reckoning. O Pen of the Most High! It is now Our wish to make mention of one of My maidservants, who hath given ear unto My Call; turned towards My horizon; inhaled the fragrance of My garment; arisen to commemorate and extol Me; circled around My Cause; sought the shelter of My presence; entered beneath the shadow of the tree of My loving-kindness; borne the trials of the world for love of Me and in My path; and cast away the vain imaginations of all peoples, through the power of My laws and precepts. She it is who, in the seat of this Resplendent Vision, was the consort of Our Name that was named 'Abdu'r-Rahím. O Samandar! By My life! We, verily, concealed his station in this vain life, and extolled him in My concealed and treasured Scroll in such wise that the hearts of them that are endued with understanding were enraptured. Blessed is he who was privileged to meet him during his days, or who visiteth him after his ascension: We testify that he is of the blissful. Blessed is he who approacheth and, standing before his grave, saith: "The peace of God, and of Them Who are His Chosen Ones, His Trustees, the Daysprings of His Revelation, the Dawning-places of His inspiration, the Manifestations of His Cause, and the Bearers of His throne, be upon thee, O thou light shining above the horizon of certitude, and blazoner of the praise of thy Lord, the Lord of all mankind! I testify that, upon hearing the Call, thou didst arise; didst answer thy Lord's summons; didst hasten with thine whole heart unto His Most Exalted Horizon and His Most Glorious Vision; and didst receive the choice wine of understanding from the hand of the bounty of thy Lord, the Mighty, the Beneficent. I testify, moreover, that thou wast steadfast in the Cause of God, in such wise that neither the clamour of the heedless, nor the blame of the ignorant, nor the estrangement of the froward, nor the protests of the malicious, nor the grunting of the wicked, nor the barking of the malevolent, could deter thee. Thou art he who was mentioned by the Pen of the Most High; was favoured with the Verses of God, the Lord of all names; and did quaff of the living waters of Divine utterance from the cup of the wisdom of God, the Lord of the worlds. I testify, furthermore, that thou didst acknowledge that which God Himself acknowledged in the Day whereon commotions seized all the dwellers of the earth, save those whom God, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise, was pleased to spare. Thou art he who heard in the path of God what none had heard, and bore in the love of God what none of His servants had borne before him. Thou art he who cast vain imaginings behind his back, and mere conjecture beneath his feet; and directed himself towards the Qiblih of the world with a heart sanctified from the insinuations of the deniers, and the whisperings of them that disbelieved in God, the Lord of the Day of Reckoning. Blessed art thou, and whoever draweth nigh unto thee, and visiteth thee where thou liest buried; and whoever remembereth thee, and that which befell thee at the hands of those who disbelieved in God, disputed His signs, eschewed His presence, protested against Him, and arose to put out His light, whereby both earth and heaven have been illumined: we testify that such, truly, are numbered with the companions of the Fire, in the Book of God, the King, the Just, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise." Now make We mention of Muhammad before 'Alí, whose name thou didst mention in thy letter; thy Lord, truly, is the Almighty, the All-Bounteous. Grieve not at thy separation from Us! He, verily, writeth down for whomsoever He willeth whatsoever He desireth; thy Lord, of a truth, is the Almighty, the Unrestrained. Let nothing grieve thee: rejoice rather in the days of thy Lord, and say: "Unto Thee be praise, O Thou Who art the Lord of earth and heaven! I testify that the earth hath been honoured with Thy footsteps; the air hath been graced with Thy sweet savours; the sun hath been illumined by the light of Thy Countenance; the heavens have been raised through Thy Will; the earth hath beamed at Thine appearance; and the world hath trembled in its yearning to meet Thee. O my Lord! I ask Thee by the wrongs Thou hast suffered to write down for me with Thy Most Exalted Pen that which beseemeth the heaven of Thy bounty and the ocean of Thy generosity. O my Lord! I bear witness that Thou hast called me, and all things, into being for the sake of attaining unto Thy presence; of appearing before the throne of Thy majesty; and of standing at the door of Thy mercy. Yet despite my knowledge of all this, and my certainty of what Thou hast deemed acceptable before Thy Countenance, wert Thou to bid me halt, I would be content with Thy behest; and wert Thou to debar me from Thy presence, I would declare: 'Praised art Thou, and obeyed in Thy command, O Thou Who holdest in Thine hand the kingdom of all things, and wieldest in Thy grasp the empire of all names! No God is there besides Thee, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise!' O my Lord! I ask Thee by those who have arisen to assist Thy Cause, and by those at whose agonies the Concourse on high, and the dwellers of the Kingdom of Names, have lamented, to write down for me with the Pen of Thy grace the recompense of meeting Thee, and the recompense of those who hastened unto the Dayspring of Thy Revelation with such eagerness that the waves of the ocean could not deter them from following Thy path, nor could the hosts of the wicked doers debar them from attaining unto the Court of Thy grace; until they entered into Thy Most Great Prison; stood before the throne; hearkened unto Thy Call; attained the lights of Thy Countenance; and clung imploringly unto the hem of Thy bestowal. O my Lord! I am poor, and Thou art the All-Possessing; and I am impotent, while Thou art the God of power. I have lifted my suppliant hands unto the heaven of Thy bounties: shouldst Thou refuse me, Thou, truly, art the best of judges; and shouldst Thou send down upon me by Thy grace what I have wished for, Thou, truly, art the best of bestowers. I testify under all conditions that Thou art to be praised in Thy doings, and to be obeyed in Thy behest. No God is there besides Thee, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise." O Pen of the Most Merciful! Make now mention of him that hath been named Hasan before Khán, that he may rejoice in My remembrance, and arise to discharge that which shall profit him in the worlds of My Cause, and in My glorious and sublime Kingdom. Be thou so steadfast that neither the events of the world nor the clamour of the nations shall deter thee; thus biddeth thee the Ancient King from this Resplendent Seat. Say: The heedless have, verily, imprisoned Him in this impregnable stronghold; yet under all conditions He summoneth the dwellers of the kingdom of creation unto God, the Creator of the heavens, albeit the people are for the most part unaware. Of them is he that hearkeneth, and of them is he that is heedless; of them is he that hearkeneth and turneth aside, and of them is he that hearkeneth and hasteneth to obey the summons of his Ancient Lord. This is a day whereon it behoveth the whole world to become a single ear, that it may hearken unto this Most Sweet Call, which hath been raised betwixt earth and heaven; thus affirmeth the Lord of all mankind in this mighty prison. Render thanks unto thy Lord, for that He hath made mention of thee in these Verses, whereby the eyes of them that are nigh unto God have been gladdened. O Husayn! The Face of this Wronged One hath turned towards thee from this Spot, and He saith: Blessed the stranger who hath recognized his most exalted home; the hearkener who hath heard the Call of the King of creation; the seer who hath beheld My Most Glorious Horizon; and the speaker who hath spoken forth My beauteous praise. This Wronged One, verily, calleth upon thee, and commendeth unto thee that which the All-Merciful hath sent down in His Wondrous Book. Cleave thou unto God and His commandments, and be thou so wedded thereto that all those whose sense of smell is keen may inhale from thee the fragrance of the love of God, the Lord of the worlds. Thus hath My Supreme Pen spoken as a bounty on its part, and I am the All-Bounteous, the Most Generous. O Samandar! It behoveth thee to render thanks and praise unto thy Lord, inasmuch as He hath sent down for each one of the names mentioned in thy letter that wherefrom the sincere will inhale the fragrance of My Revelation, and the perfume of My resplendent garment. The Glory of God rest upon thee, and upon them, and upon him that attained the honour of meeting and of serving Me, who is indeed none other but 'Alí after Nabíl. We, verily, make mention of him at the end of this Epistle, that he may rejoice in the remembrance of his Lord, the Lord of Utterance, the All-Informed. Over his countenance do We cast a salutation from this Spot, recalling the days when he stood before the throne, and hearkened unto the Call of his Lord, the Almighty, the All-Praised. The Glory of God rest upon thee, and upon him, and upon your two families and those that are with you both, and upon those that have believed in God, the Lord of the Mighty Throne. Praise be to God, the Lord of the worlds.

He it Is That Is Manifest, and Speaketh Forth, above the Supreme Horizon

This is an Epistle from Us unto such as have cast away the world, and laid hold on whatsoever He Who is the Most Great Name hath revealed in this Day whereon the Crier hath cried out from the right hand of the snow-white Spot, announcing that the tale of sorrows hath been retold, in such wise that the Apostle hath lamented in the All-highest Paradise, and the Virgin hath wept beside the Sadratu'l-Muntahá: thus hath it been decreed by God, the Lord of Names and the Creator of the heavens, in a Scroll whereof none is informed save God, the Lord of the worlds. He it is, in truth, Who speaketh forth from His Most Great Prison, testifying to that whereunto God Himself had testified ere the creation of all things, and ere the creation of earth and heaven. O ye beloved of the All-Merciful throughout the world! By My life! The morn of utterance hath broken, and the sun of testimony hath shone with such splendour that none save those who have disbelieved in God, the Exalted, the Great, hath denied it. Although beset by sorrows on every hand, yet is the Tongue engaged in utterance; while the Pen of the Most High moveth and courseth in the arena of wisdom and understanding with such impetuosity that neither the hosts of the world, nor the imaginations of the ignorant who, without any clear proof or Book from God, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise, pretend to learning, can arrest it. Consider ye the people and their actions. They lament and weep at that which befell the Holy Family aforetime, disavowing all connection with those who wronged them; yet perpetrate their selfsame actions, albeit they comprehend it not. The Concourse on high have stood aghast at their actions, and the Most Great Spirit and the inmates of Paradise have lamented, yet the people perceive it not. They have given themselves up to their passions, turning aside from God, the Help in Peril, the Self-Subsisting. Thus hath this Wronged One spoken, and sent down unto you that wherefrom ye may inhale the sweet savour of God, the All-Powerful, the Loving. He, verily, loveth his loved ones, and watcheth over them from this forbidden Spot. Hearken now in the Persian tongue unto the Call of Him Whom the world hath wronged, during these days when the dark clouds of oppression have prevented the resplendent face of the daystar of justice from shedding forth its light, and when the dove of equity is sore tried in the clutches of tyranny; that perchance ye may know with absolute certainty that the trials of earth and heaven cannot restrain the Pen of the Most High from extolling God and from celebrating His praise. Under all conditions it is occupied with the mention of Him Who is the All-Possessing, the Most High, that perchance even one of the peoples of the earth may inhale the fragrance of the utterance of the All-Merciful, and remain not deprived of the living ocean which hath been manifested in the name of Him Who is the Best-Beloved of all men. O friends! Although the calamity that hath befallen was, and is, most grievous, yet is He who created them well able to create others like unto them; He, verily, is the Almighty, the Most Powerful. Ye must, by the grace of God, be so steadfast in the Cause that the vicissitudes of temporal existence shall not debar you from the eternal kingdom. The earth is even such as ye have witnessed and do now witness, and no discerning person, who hath fixed his gaze upon the Most Sublime Vision, hath ever been, or ever shall be, deceived as to its true nature, inasmuch as at every moment he beholdeth how one group arriveth and another group departeth. Wherefore 'tis certain that no right-minded person hath ever been, or ever shall be, kept back thereby from the One True God. Strive that haply ye may become a means of quickening this wilting world with a new spirit. Thus commandeth you this Wronged One from this far-distant Spot. He that directed himself hither, and attained unto the presence of his Lord, made mention of you before the throne, whence We have made mention of you as a bounty on Our part, and I am the Rememberer, the All-Knowing. All of you are present before the Eye of God: He, verily, witnesseth and seeth, and He, truly, is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing. Rejoice ye at this Most Great Remembrance; then give praise unto your Lord, the All-Merciful, at every moment. The Glory of God rest upon you, inasmuch as ye hearkened, yet forbore; beheld, yet forewent; and witnessed that which none hath witnessed in the path of God, the All-Possessing, the All-Highest, the Ever Forgiving, the Most Bountiful. The world and all that is therein shall pass away, while that which hath been destined for you shall endure; thereto shall your names and your works be exalted on earth: thus informeth you He Who is the Truthful, the Trustworthy.

He is the All-Glorious, the Incomparable

The Bird of the Throne hath taken flight at the croaking of the raven; thy Lord, verily, is the All-Glorious, the All-Knowing. O Muhammad before Ridá! We, verily, make mention of thee in this Spot, that thou mayest rejoice at this remembrance, through which the ocean of faith hath surged, and the fragrance of the mercy of thy Lord, the Lord of Revelation, hath been wafted. Beware lest aught withhold thee from God, the Creator of the heavens! God is My witness! The Word of thy Lord is such as all the treasures of the earth can never equal: unto this testifieth He through Whom the kingdom of utterance hath been made manifest in the world of being. Although beset by sorrows on every hand, the All-Merciful yet calleth out: "No God is there but Him, the Almighty, the Unrestrained!" Naught hath prevented Him from achieving His purpose: He ordaineth as He pleaseth through the power of His sovereignty; He, of a truth, is the One, the All-Seeing. The oppressors have slain the sons of the Prophet, then make mention of Him at eventide and at dawn. The kingdoms of earth and heaven have stood bewildered at their actions. Erelong shall the blasts of chastisement overtake them from all sides: He, verily, shall lay hold upon them even as He laid hold upon others before them. Consider those who imprisoned Us in the most desolate of cities! Blessed is he that readeth the Lawh-i-Ra'ís, and learneth what proceeded from the Pen of the Most High when He was a captive in the hands of the wicked doers. The Glory of God be upon thee, and upon thy father, and upon those who have clung to the hem of grace, and have acknowledged that which God hath Himself acknowledged both in the beginning and in the end.

In the Name of Him Who is Almighty and Most Powerful

Thy letter arrived and was perused in its entirety. The people have perpetrated an injustice such as to cast the kingdoms of earth and heaven into despondency, while the Twin Lights have manifested a degree of meekness under tribulation such that the dwellers of the heavenly realm have bewailed and lamented them. Consider thou the son of Zakaríyyá, who lost his head to please the courtesan of the era; and again the scion of the Prophet, who was slaughtered at the behest of the wastrel of the age: was it they who were martyred that lost, or was it those who wronged them? -- in reply to which all things have cried out, exclaiming: "Yea, the latter are in perspicuous loss!" Although this calamity is most grievous, and the greatest abasement hath been witnessed on its account, yet, by the righteousness of God, is it in reality the mightiest honour, which hath but outwardly assumed the form of an abasement. Do thou preserve this lofty and most exalted station, nor have regard for that which is today apparent. God, verily, hath laid hold on wrongdoers in the past, and shall do so in the future; and He shall purge the earth of their like, and so raise up your station that all faces shall turn towards you, and all the tongues of the world shall recite your praise. Hearken thou unto the Call of this Wronged One, and lay fast hold on all that He hath mentioned. He, verily, is the Faithful Counsellor. See that thou spare no effort in doing all thou canst to protect the people's claims upon the King of Martyrs, forasmuch as this matter is acceptable and pleasing in the sight of God, and a cause of exaltation and advancement. Do thou on behalf of this Wronged One make mention of all the relatives, and speak unto them words of consolation. He, verily, is the Comforter, the All-Knowing. God willing, thou wilt remain, as heretofore, beneath the glances of God's loving providence. Rest assured, and be thou of the thankful. That which is incumbent upon thee is to ensure the contentment of the family of the Twin Martyrs -- may the Glory of God rest upon them. Wert thou to ponder a while, thou wouldst know of a certainty that what hath befallen is, and ever shall be, an inestimable honour. Unto this testifieth He Who hath knowledge of the Book. Praise be to God, the Lord of Lords.

In the Name of the One, All-Seeing God

O My leaf, and the leaf of My Divine Lote Tree! The winds of malice have arisen, and from the Lote Tree of the Cause have fallen leaves for whom the Beloved (Muhammad) hath lamented, the Friend (Abraham) hath cried out, and Gabriel hath announced: "The torment hath been made ready for you, O ye people of malice!" Please God, thou wilt attain unto His special favour, and find solace in the remembrance of Him. Notwithstanding that this supreme calamity transcendeth all calamities, yet did the best of mortals lose his head and lay down his life in the way of the Ancient King. Although outwardly this matter seareth the heart, yet is it, and shall it ever be, the means and cause of the growth of the Divine Lote Tree. I swear by the Daystar of Truth, which today shineth above the horizon of the Revelation, that were the full glory of this station to be disclosed, all the friends would direct themselves towards the place of sacrifice, nor accept a ransom. Thy letter arrived and was perused. Thou hast ever been, and shalt ever be, beneath the glances of the gracious providence of the True One; and whatsoever wisdom dictateth, the same shall flow forth from the heaven of God's Command. Rejoice thou in My Revelation; in My stablishment upon the throne; in My Call; in My remembrance; and in My praise. Thy Lord, truly, is the Ever-Observant, the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing. His honour the Afnán -- upon him be of all glories the Most Glorious -- is present before My Face, and God sendeth down from the heaven of His bounty that which hath been destined for him. He, verily, is the Most Gracious, the All-Bountiful. Be thou in no wise sorrowed, and hold fast, as bidden, unto the cord of patience. He, verily, will make manifest that which shall rejoice the hearts of those who have been afflicted with sorrows by reason of that which the hands of rebellion have wrought. He, verily, is the Almighty, the Most Powerful. The Glory of God rest upon you all, and upon those maidservants who have believed in Him Who is the Incomparable, the All-Knowing.

He is the Most Holy, the Most Great

Say: Glory be to Thee, O God, the Lord of all things, and Creator of all Names! I ask Thee by that Name whereby all idols have been shattered, and through which all vain imaginations have passed away, to immerse me in the ocean of certitude, O Thou Who art the Lord of Revelation! O my Lord! Assist me to perform that which Thou hast desired, through the power of Thy sovereignty, and which Thou hast sent down in Thine unerring Book. O my Lord! This is a day wherewith the Scriptures of the world, and the Books which Thou didst send down upon Thy Messengers and Thy Chosen Ones, have been adorned. I beseech Thee not to deprive me of the drops sprinkled by the ocean of Thy grace, nor to cast me out of the door which Thou hast opened before all who are in Thy heaven and all who are on Thine earth. O my Lord! I am weak: yet have I laid hold upon Thy Name, the Powerful, the Mighty. Do Thou destine for me by Thy grace that which shall profit me both in this world and in the world to come. Thou, verily, art the Great Giver, the All-Bountiful, the Most Powerful, the All-Glorious, the All-Wise.

He is the Most Holy, the Most Great

O Varqá! The servant in attendance hath come before Us, and presented that which thou didst set forth in thy letter. We, truly, found it to be a mirror reflective of thy love for Him Who is the Beloved of the world, and of thy turning unto Him. Blessed art thou, inasmuch as thou hast drawn nigh, hast quaffed thy fill, and hast attained unto thine object. Thy Lord, verily, is the Expounder, the Most Manifest. We have beheld the fire that hath surrounded thee in the love of thy Lord, and We have seen its blaze and heard its roaring. Exalted be He Who ignited it, Who kindled it and Who brought it into being! He, verily, is the Almighty, before the revelation of Whose power the very essence of power hath confessed its impotence. Thy Lord, verily, heareth and seeth; He truly is the All-Informed. Rejoice thou for that this Wronged One remembereth thee, as He hath remembered thee aforetime, and as He doth so now, while He paceth, saying: "I have perceived the fragrance of thy love, and have observed thy sincerity and thy submissiveness whensoe'er thine heart is occupied with My remembrance, and thy tongue engaged in speaking forth My beauteous praise." Thus hath the Ocean of Life imparted a sprinkling of its moisture, that thou mayest rejoice during the days of thy Lord, the Almighty, the Wondrous. O Varqá! Thy call was heard, and thy letter was presented before the throne. Praise be to God! The brands of the love of God were perceived therefrom. Please God, thou wilt ever continue, as heretofore, to delight in the mention of the Beloved, to drink in His Name, to rest in His remembrance, and to be occupied with the thought of Him, that perchance the remote may draw nigh unto the ocean of nearness, and the languid may be stimulated by the heat of the Divine Word to hasten unto that quarter which is sanctified above all other quarters. Some of those whose hearts are turned towards Him appear to have been saddened, nay affrighted, by the incident that hath transpired in the Land of Sád; whereas in reality all that hath befallen is that the Hand of Divine power hath, as a special favour, raised them up, and, from the heaven of mercy and the cloud of bounty, rained down upon them showers of grace and blessing. His consummate power hath adorned them amongst all people with the ornament of honour, whence their praise is now sung by the tongues of the sincere, and of all such as have drawn nigh unto God. They attained a station such that even their enemies testified to the loftiness of their rank; while at the end of their days they attained the most sublime and lofty of all stations, which is that of Supreme Sacrifice. This is a station which the saints and chosen ones of God have from everlasting sought and hoped for, as they do so still, and shall for evermore. This notwithstanding, some appear to be dejected and despondent. God willing, such feelings have arisen out of love for them. I swear by the ocean of true understanding that were the station of one of their servants, who is even now engaged in service, to be revealed, the peoples of the earth would be astounded. Blessed is he who pondereth over what hath come to pass, that he may become acquainted with the greatness of the Cause, and its sovereign might. This station which they attained they themselves had craved of the True One -- exalted and glorified be He -- and had sought and hoped for with the utmost fervour and longing. Say: O friends! Much have ye suffered for the love of Him Who is the Beloved of the worlds! Ye have witnessed, and seen, that which it was not meet should be seen, and ye have heard that which it was not fitting should be heard. In the pathway of the Friend, ye have borne things that were in truth more crushing than the mountains. Blessed be your backs, your eyes, and your ears, for that which they have borne, seen, and heard. Now, do ye appreciate the excellence of this lofty and most exalted station, and see that ye do naught to dim its lustre. Whate'er betide, the claws of death shall fasten upon this perishable world, and all that are in it; while whatsoever it containeth shall be afflicted in the clutches of change. Do ye beseech at all times the One True God -- exalted and glorified be He -- to preserve you, and to keep you steadfast upon His Straight Path. Know ye this much, that whatsoever ye have borne, or seen and heard, for His sake, the same is but a token of His grace and loving providence, wherewith ye have been especially favoured. This mention of you that He maketh in the Tablets is, and ever shall be, another instance of His grace. Ye have tasted of the chalice of affliction in His path: quaff ye then the choicest wine from the goblets of His mention and His favours. Please God, ye will be graciously enabled to serve the Cause; thereto We commend unto all a praiseworthy character, goodly deeds, and a seemly and acceptable demeanour. In this day, it is incumbent upon everyone to cleave, and have recourse, to whatsoever shall exalt the Cause of God. Say: This much We say, and for the rest leave it to your sense of equity to judge what should befit a day such as this. Be ye not saddened by outward frailty, abasement and disarray. I swear by the daystar of the heaven of self-sufficiency that honour and riches circle around you, sing your praise, and incline in your direction.
