If, pursuant to the dictates of Divine wisdom, the appearance thereof should remain for a few days hidden, yet days shall come when each one of you will appear manifest and resplendent as the sun. We beseech the One True God that the people may discover the sweetness of the Divine utterances, and truly savour it. The Glory of Our presence rest upon thee, and upon thy brother, and upon My Name who laid down his life in My path, and hath rested in the precincts of My mercy. We, verily, mention at the end of this Epistle thy brother, who hath turned his face unto My Face, stood before the door of My majesty, and hearkened unto My mighty and wondrous Call. God willing, that which hath been mentioned will not depart from his eyes: he will rest assured in the loving providence of God, quaff at all times the choice wine of His remembrance, and fix his gaze upon His court. God willing, the matter of love and unity also will not be overlooked. We make mention at this juncture of him that hath been named Kázim, that he may rejoice in the remembrance of God, the Most Exalted, the Most Great. Blessed art thou, and thy brother, who was martyred in the path of God, the Lord of the worlds. Consider thou, and bethink thee of, Our servant Kázim who suffered in the Land of Sád a martyrdom so grievous that all the atoms of the universe, and beyond them the Concourse on high and the dwellers of the Cities of Names, bewailed his agony. Unto this testifieth thy Lord, the Witness, the All-Informed. O Kázim! Reflect thou upon the loving providence of the True One; behold His mercy, which hath encompassed all peoples; and contemplate that blessed Word which was sent down in the Epistle to Há' and Sín. He said, and truly did He speak: "Whoso is for God, God is for him." Since, therefore, it was in the pathway of the King of eternal glory that those sanctified souls renounced the world and all its peoples, and won the cup of martyrdom -- which is in reality the winning arrow -- for this reason is the Pen of the Most High seen at each dawn and eventide to be occupied with their remembrance, and restless in its exposition of this theme. I swear by the sun of the kingdom of utterance that if the shrilling voice of the Pen of the Most High were truly hearkened unto with a listening ear, all would hasten forth from their habitations, and cry aloud "Here am I, O Lord my God, here am I!" Blessed the ear that hath hearkened; the heart that hath apprehended that which hath flowed forth; and the palate that hath savoured all that hath been made manifest of the loving-kindness of thy Lord, the Ever-Forgiving, the Most Bountiful. O Kázim! Do even as thou hast been bidden, and thou shalt behold the loving-kindness of thy Lord, which pervadeth all the worlds. The Glory of God be upon thee, and upon those who have attained the bounty of manifesting the Most Great Steadfastness in this Cause, through which the mountains have been scattered in dust, the heavens have been cleft asunder, the earth hath been rent in twain, and all God's servants have trembled, save only those whom God, the Almighty, the Protector, the Powerful, was pleased to spare.

He is the Most Holy, the Most Glorious

A remembrance from Us unto him that hath hearkened unto My Call, and whose response to the Lord of all mankind We have heard, that he may be overtaken by the joy born of Mine utterance, notwithstanding that sorrows have encompassed the entire creation. O thou proclaimer of My Cause, and beholder of My Countenance! Grieve not at that which hath befallen the Cause: thy Lord, truly, lieth in wait. He shall lay hold on the wrongdoers, even as He laid hold on him that was their chief; He, truly, is severe in punishing! They have kindled with their own hands the fire of affliction; yet are the people in a wondrous stupor! So besotted have they become in the drunkenness of their evil passions that they have perpetrated that whereat the cloud hath cried out. Say: Was it Hasan who disbelieved in God, or was it that which he possessed? If it was he, why then didst thou pillage his possessions, O thou false dissembler? Think they that they will consume what they have amassed? Nay, by Him Who is the Lord of Lords! They have committed that whereat the inmates of the Kingdom have lamented, and beyond them the Day of Reckoning. O My companion! Consider thou, and reflect upon, the grace of God, and His loving-kindness. He, verily, raised them up in truth, and adorned them with the best of ornaments. He so ennobled them that men's tongues spake forth their praise; He honoured them with that Supreme Sacrifice which hath from everlasting been the hope of them that have drawn nigh unto Him; and the Pen of God hath been moved to commemorate them in such wise that all hearts have melted. The servant in attendance hath come before Our Countenance, and read out that wherewith thou didst call upon this Wronged One; and We have answered thee with this Epistle. Beware lest aught sadden thee; thereto admonish My branches, and those who have sought My Countenance, that it may bring them joy after their sorrows. The Glory of God rest upon thee, and upon whosoever reflecteth upon that which hath been revealed by God, the Lord of the Return. This is that which was sent down in reply from God, the Almighty, the Most Bountiful. O Javád! The epistle which his honour 'Alí before Akbar -- upon him be the Glory of God -- wrote unto thee was presented in its entirety before the Divine Countenance by the servant in attendance, and granted the honour of an attentive hearing. The beginning of the letter was adorned with expressions of homage, praise, gratitude and thanksgiving unto Him Who is the Beloved of the world. Blessed the tongue that hath in this day made mention of Him; the heart that hath attained unto His love; the eyes that have been privileged to behold the Most Sublime Vision; the face that hath turned unto the Face of God, the Supreme Ordainer; and the Pen that hath been moved to extol and to praise Him. Thus hath My Most Exalted Pen spoken in this noble habitation. Howbeit certain remarks were observed at the end thereof which bespoke feelings of sorrow, and were unworthy of these days; among others the following expressions had been employed: "...especially in these days when God hath so willed it that these servants should become the objects of whatever trials descend and calamities befall." He had likewise used other expressions yet more grievous, or at least similar, in tenor. Yea, in the path of God the believers have been imprisoned; taunted by their enemies; and afflicted by calamities. Yet all these matters do not equal a single letter of the Verses which had erewhile been sent down from the Dayspring of God's loving-kindness especially for him, and for those who had been privileged to suffer calamities in My path; and which We had ordered the servant in attendance, after having written them out, to despatch from hence. How strange that, after hearkening unto those Verses, whose fragrance hath intoxicated and delighted the Concourse on high, he should have occupied himself with such expressions, and sent them to the Holy Land! By the righteousness of God! All that hath been created on earth doth not equal a single letter thereof! Were that Tablet to be recited before those who are nigh unto God, and truly devoted to His Cause, they would of a surety be so inebriated by the choice wine of the All-Merciful as to renounce the world and all its peoples; and had they eternity to live, then ever, so long as life endured, would they repeat: "Praise be to Thee!" "Glory be to Thee!" "Thanks be to Thee!" and "Bounty be to Thee!" Although the incident of the Land of Sád was a cause and occasion for the hearts of them that are nigh unto God, and of the sanctified, to be consumed, yet had it been imagined that, after witnessing the sun-like favours shining above the horizon of the gracious providence of the Pen of God, all would beseech and hope that they too might attain unto a dewdrop from this same ocean. In such days as these it behoveth one who, like his honour, hath ever been under the glances of God's loving-kindness, and hath attained unto a position of nearness, to speak such words as shall cause tepid souls to be set on fire, and occasion tranquillity to troubled hearts. In days gone by many such matters took place -- nay, yet more grievous and distressful -- as he himself hath seen and heard. A considerable period hath now elapsed during which the like events have but seldom come to pass; this notwithstanding, most seem perturbed, affrighted, confused and sorrowful. These Twin Luminaries, meaning Há' and Há', bent their course towards 'Iráq; attained the ocean of God's presence; and drank their fill of the living waters of reunion. In those days they were unknown, save to a handful of souls; but after being graced by God's bountiful favour they became known and celebrated among the whole company of those who are nigh unto Him, and truly devoted to His Cause, nay among the Celestial Concourse itself. At the end of their days they attained unto that Supreme Sacrifice which, in their letters to the True One -- exalted and glorified be He -- they themselves had sought and hoped for; while touching that which befell them, words were sent down from the Pen of the Most High that shall abide and endure for as long as the kingdoms of earth and heaven shall last. By thy life, O 'Alí! This is a cause for thanks -- but thanks of a kind wherefrom the very ocean of good pleasure is apparent. The groaning and lamentation of the Pen of the Most High have been, and ever shall be, in token of His loving-kindness, His grace, and His fidelity; for otherwise the Divine Lote Tree is exalted through the blood of His chosen ones. In fine, abasement in My path is the king of honours; poverty in My love hath ever been, and ever shall be, the prince of riches; and death in My good pleasure is the dawning-place of life. Take good heed, then, O ye who are endued with understanding hearts; and mark ye well that which hath been uttered, O ye who are endued with vision!

In a Blessed Tablet addressed to Hakím Áqá Ján Tabíb-i-Hamadání, the Ancient Beauty -- exalted be His glory -- says the following:

For whatever property hath been plundered in the Land of Sád, and for each drop of blood that hath been unjustly shed therein, innumerable souls have departed from this world, and shall depart hereafter, and so likewise with respect to possessions. Sleep hath not overtaken the One True God, nor ever shall it. He is awake and aware, and the wrongdoers shall assuredly taste the bitter fruits of their actions. Through the appearance of but one of the deeds of the She-Serpent, the second 'Ubaydu'lláh hath been made manifest; and he hath committed that wherefrom the first 'Ubaydu'lláh shrank. "God's malison upon the people of tyranny!" Naught hath betided in this world, nor ever shall it, without an attendant cause and fruit. Reflect thou how many souls have perished, and how many lands and cities have returned to dust, whereof naught is now seen but a level plain. The lot of today is even this; and hereafter the True One knoweth what shall come to pass. Nor think that, in the midst of this, the friends of God have been slain by the swords of the oppressors. I swear by the sun of the kingdom of truthfulness that each one of the friends of God who quaffed in that incident the draft of martyrdom ascended unto the throne of the Most High, and rested and reposed beneath the shade of the canopy of Divine mercy. Were those stations to reveal their splendour to the extent even of a needle's eye, all would raise the cry "Would I had been with him!" Whatsoever outward loss hath been sustained by any of the friends, the same was then, and remaineth now, pure gain. The people of Bahá have ever been, as they are today, assured of mighty gain. If, pursuant to the dictates of Divine wisdom, for a fleeting day, or over a certain limited period, some loss should be incurred, it behoveth not to grieve thereat. Assuredly the One True God shall adorn it with the ornament of the greatest gain. He, verily, is the True One, and He is the All-Powerful, the All-Knowing, and the All-Wise.

In a Tablet addressed to their honours the Afnáns, the Ancient Beauty -- exalted be His Glory -- says:

O My Name! The incident of the Land of Sád is remembered before the Countenance of God as among the greatest of calamities, whence till now well nigh a hundred Tablets have been revealed from the world of Divine providence, and flowed forth from the Pen of the Most High, in remembrance of him, and of those who were with him. No one hath attained unto such an outpouring of grace. Unto this testifieth that which the Most Merciful hath sent down in the Tablets. By Thy might! The inmates of My Kingdom and My Realm of Glory, and the dwellers of the Tabernacle of My Holiness, have bewailed and lamented his and their sufferings. Howbeit this blessed Word appeared aforetime from the Dayspring of God's Light:

> O ransom of God! Shouldst thou be slain for love *
>
> Flinch not, and yield thy soul for the sake of love!

Whatsoever befell those consecrated souls in the way of God hath assuredly not been without effect, and the fruit thereof will assuredly appear. Do thou inform My branches of that whereof thou hast been informed by Him Who is the All-Informed.

Section Six

Tablets Revealed in Honour of the Relatives

Of the Twin Shining Lights

O Ibráhím! Hearken thou unto the Call of thy Lord, the All-Glorious, which hath been raised from His most sublime and lofty Station. He, verily, will confirm thee in that which beseemeth the days of thy Lord, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise. Thou art he who directed his steps towards the Supreme Horizon, and who visited the Spot wherein the Tongue of Grandeur hath spoken: "The Kingdom is God's, the Lord of the worlds!" Blessed is every face that hath turned unto the Face of God; and the heart that hath attained unto His love, the Most Precious. Lay thou hold upon the Sure Handle, and say: "O Lord of the throne above and of earth below! I ask Thee by Thy Name through which the Supreme Horizon hath been illumined, to assist me to serve Thee in such wise that I may move according to Thy will, and breathe by Thy leave and at Thy pleasure. Thou, verily, art the Almighty, before Whom all things have bowed; and the Sovereign to Whom all that are in heaven and on earth have submitted. O my Lord! Behold Thou Thy lovers in Thy lands, who have trembled at the onslaught of Thine enemies. I beseech Thee, by the light of Thy Countenance and the fire of Thy love, so to attract them by Thine utterance that they may not be affected by Thine enemies, and by the estrangement of the learned amongst Thy creatures who pretend to knowledge without any clear proof from Thee, or testimony on Thy part. O my Lord! I am a suppliant, and Thou art the Answerer of prayers; and I am a poor creature, and Thou art the All-Possessing. Deal with me then as befitteth Thy majesty and Thy sovereignty. Thou, truly, art the Almighty, the Most Powerful."

He is the Expounder, the All-Knowing, the All-Wise

O Ibráhím! Hearken thou unto the call of the Friend (Abraham): He, of a truth, crieth out to thee from this Vale which hath been named "Nabíl" in the Book of God, the Lord of the worlds. He, verily, remembereth thee as a bounty on His part, that thou mayest make good what hath escaped thee in the days of God, the Almighty, the All-Wise. Reflect thou upon that which hath been manifested in truth, and say: "I ask Thee, O Thou Maker of the heavens and Lord of all names, by Thy Name whereby Thou hast subdued all things, to grant that I may understand that from which the learned of the lands and the wise of Thy realm have been veiled. O my Lord! I am the one whom Thou didst cause to hearken unto Thy Most Exalted Call when it was raised from Thy Most Sublime Horizon; yet interposing veils prevented me from turning with my whole being unto Thee: wherefore I was deprived of the soft-flowing stream of Thine utterance, and the living waters of Thy knowledge. O my God, O my God! Thy grace is my highest aspiration, and Thy forgiveness my fondest hope, my deepest longing, and my dearest wish. I ask Thee by the sun of Thy bounty and the ocean of Thy bestowal graciously to aid me to accomplish that which is pleasing and acceptable unto Thee. Potent art Thou to do what pleaseth Thee. Thou holdest in Thine hands the reins of all things. No God is there but Thee, the Ever-Forgiving, the All-Bounteous." O Ibráhím! Wert thou, rid of attachment unto all things, to cry out but once, assuredly thou wouldst hear the response. Today, the heaven of Divine bounty hath been raised, and assuredly if a soul but turn unto God in a befitting manner he shall not remain deprived. I commend unto thee that wherewith the One True God -- exalted be His glory -- hath admonished His servants in all the Holy Scriptures. Do thou lay aside whatsoever preventeth thee from recognizing God and His Cause. O Ibráhím! Cast off thy self, then turn with thine whole heart unto the horizon through which the faces of the sincere have been illumined. This is the Day whose station hath been mentioned and set down in all the Holy Books. Should any matter escape one, never shall he be able to make it good! Close thine eyes to the people, that thou mayest behold the Face of the Loved One, abiding after the evanescence of all things. By the righteousness of God! Great, immeasurably great is this Cause; and He that admonisheth thee wholly for the sake of God is, verily, the Faithful Counsellor. Strive thou that the clay clods of the earth may not deprive thee of the blooms of Divine mysteries. Truly, it is a matter of astonishment that although none is informed of the root of this Cause, yet whatsoever is manifest among the people deriveth from this station, pursuant to a wisdom whereof none hath been informed save Him Who is the All-Informed; howbeit most people have remained deprived and oblivious thereof. Say: O servants! The darkness of your deeds hath obscured the world. Strive ye to attain unto the true brightness. Of a certainty words can never take the place of deeds. Cling ye to goodly and praiseworthy deeds, and purge and sanctify yourselves from the defilement of whatsoever is subject to the Divine prohibitions, in order that ye may attain unto true composure. By My life! I speak not from mere impulse: unto this testifieth all who have been ennobled by the quality of fair-mindedness in the kingdom of creation. Peace be upon whosoever followeth the way of guidance, and pondereth upon all matters. Do thou embrace whatsoever shall draw thee nigh unto the Straight Path of God.

*His honour Mírzá Sádiq, upon him be the Glory of God*

He is God, exalted be He; grandeur and utterance are His estate. Sád, Dál, Qáf. The memorial of the mercy of God unto the one who quaffed the choice wine of belief, and turned unto the horizon of Him Who is the Most Compassionate, holding fast unto His cord, clinging to the hem of His robe, steadfastly serving His Cause, and gazing upon the lights of His Countenance, until he arrived in His presence, and attained unto that which the Most Compassionate hath sent down in the Furqán, and in the Evangel, the Torah and the Psalms. The Tongue of Grandeur testifieth, of Himself and by Himself, that there is no God but Him, the Help in Peril, the Self-Subsisting. He hath come down from the heaven of Proof with the standards of Perspicuous Utterance. Blessed be whoever witnesseth, and answereth His summons, and woe betide every heedless one, shut out as by a veil! O thou who hast come before this Wronged One, and dwellest now in His vicinity! He, verily, beareth witness that thou hast attained unto the Divine presence, and set thyself towards the True One at a time when all men have turned aside, except such as God, the Lord of all that was and shall be, was pleased to guide. Thou hast directed thy footsteps unto the Furthermost Goal and the Loftiest Summit, and hast soared up on the wings of detachment to the Lord of all creation, until thou didst stand before a Gate that hath been flung open before the dwellers of both the seen and the unseen realms. Render thou thanks unto God for that the Pen of the Most High so testifieth of thee on this moonlit night, when the Wronged One is seated upon His throne, and uttereth that which draweth the people nigh unto a glorious station. Blessed art thou, inasmuch as thou hast chosen thy destination, and set out upon thy journey, in such wise that neither the vagaries of the rulers nor the veils of the learned could deter thee; and hast left thy home trusting wholly in God, thy Lord, the All-Glorious, the All-Loving. We pray God to confirm and assist thee to do that which is pleasing and acceptable unto Him; and to cause to appear from thee in the world that which shall last as long as His Most Excellent Names and His Most Exalted Attributes shall last. Powerful is He to do that which He pleaseth through His word "Be," and it is. Praise be to God that thou hast hearkened, hast attained, and hast set thyself towards Him at a time when all have risen up to oppose Him. I beseech the One True God graciously to assist thee to preserve this most exalted station. He is the Almighty, the Most Powerful. The letter his honour Amín -- upon whom be My glory and My loving-kindness -- sent to thee was perused. The love and affection he expressed for thee and the members of thy household occasioned joy and gladness. We pray God to assist and succour him. He, verily, is the Most Gracious, the All-Bountiful. In truth, his honour Amín is steadfast in faith, and constant in rendering service. Blessed are they who are adorned with the adornment of love for the Twin Martyrs, for thee, and for thy kindred. Ye, verily, have an eminent position in the sight of God, the Lord of the worlds. Blessed be whoever turneth towards you; attaineth the bounty of your love; and heareth that which your tongue uttereth concerning the Cause of God, the Almighty, the All-Wise. The Glory of Our presence rest upon you, and upon Amín, and upon all that are staunch and steadfast, and all that are unwaveringly firm in their belief, and faithful to their trust.

In the Name of God, the Lord of the Kingdom of Power and Might

Praise be to God, the All-praised King, the Lord of the heavens of grace and bounty, Who created all existence; brought forth the mysteries of the unseen into the world of the seen; vouchsafed unto the people the promise of the Signal Day; and announced unto them the tidings of the appearance of the Promised Hour. When the veil was rent asunder; the secret of the Return was revealed; the veil of concealment was removed from the face of the mysteries of the Beginning in the Day of Turning back; and the realities of knowledge, as imparted in the Holy Scriptures and the Book of God, were sent down from Him Who is the Almighty, the All-Bounteous, the hearts of those endued with understanding were drawn towards the Lord of the Day of Reckoning so that they penetrated, through the power of the Sovereign Ordainer and the Creator of mankind, the Most Great Veil; turned with their whole hearts unto the most manifest yet abstruse Mystery; recognized the most sublime Embellished Symbol; and discerned Thy glorious, Thy most hidden, Thy most manifest, and Thy most resplendent Beauty. When, with nimble steps, they circled about this fire, and, through the power of Him Who is the Lord of the heaven of might, obtained their share of illumination from the lights of the Lote Tree of the Cause, the hearts of the wicked trembled, and, raising aloft the standards of hate and enmity toward God's righteous servants, they forbade them from directing their steps towards their Lord, the Almighty, the Unconstrained. Say: For how long will ye thus speed through the wildernesses of your idle fancies? The Hidden Secret hath been made manifest; the veil hath been lifted from the face of the Treasured Symbol; and the cloud hath been dispelled from before the beauty of the Preserved Light. Is it passion that hath kept you back from Him Who is the Lord of this world and of the next? Do ye protest against the people of perception because they have directed themselves towards their Lord, the Sovereign Liege of all men? Should the people of discernment hesitate to approach the precincts of that sanctuary wherein lieth their salvation? Nay, by Him from Whom is the beginning, and unto Whom is the return! Can anyone intimidate the truly pious? Say: Do ye threaten them with affliction in the path of God, the Lord of all names? These, verily, are a people who have accepted trials and tribulations; and who, in their eagerness to gain admission into the kingdom of eternity, have welcomed with their breasts the shafts of the enemies' assault. I swear by the Lord of creation! Such presumption on your part portendeth naught but heedlessness and loss. Should ye, with the swords of hatred and oppression, hew into pieces the bodies of them that gain admission into the heaven of belief, still would ye be unable to hinder them from following the way of certitude. Say: The Path hath appeared; the Proof hath been perfected; and the thirsty one hath hastened unto the stream of knowledge flowing from the Eye of Sád, which welleth out beneath the throne of Him who is the Lord of the Day of Return. Blessed are ye, O people of affection, for that ye have entered the Tabernacle of Holiness in the Kingdom of Righteousness. Through your steadfastness the hearts of the people of malice have trembled, and through your constancy upon the path of the Cause the limbs of the people of oppression and mischief have quaked. O my God, my Possessor, and my King! There is no land throughout Thy dominions that hath not been dyed crimson with the blood of Thy chosen ones, nor any tree that hath not been honoured with the bodies of Thy saints. They have borne that which hath caused the tears of the dwellers of the Tabernacle of Thy glory to flow at even and at morn; and they have suffered at the hands of the heedless that which hath caused the eyes of all who are in the heaven of Thy Cause to weep sore at daybreak and at dusk. Thou well knowest that they have harboured no purpose in Thy realm except to eradicate sedition from among Thy servants; to adorn their bodies with the robes of love and unity; and to crown their heads with the diadems of harmony and affection. For Thou hast not enjoined upon them in this Dispensation but to exhaust their energies in removing hate and rancour, and to expend their efforts in eliminating dissension, and in promoting love and unity throughout all regions. Amongst the people are those who protested against them for turning towards Thee, and for seeking illumination from the light of Thy knowledge; who passed upon them the sentence of impiety and misbelief; and who pronounced lawful the shedding of their blood, thereby rebelling against Thy sovereignty, and grievously transgressing against Thy subjects. Amongst them are those who accused them of wreaking disorder throughout the lands, thereby causing them to become victims of adversity, and objects of alternating happiness and distress. Thou dost bear witness -- yea all the atoms of the earth attest -- that never was it their intention to wreak disorder in Thy realm; and that they have not walked but in the pathway of Thy Cause, which is even for them to be united upon Thine earth, and to love their fellows among Thy creatures. Do their patience over successive years; their endurance of every hardship; their obedience of every order, not yet suffice? I swear by Thine own exalted Self, and by Thy proof which prevaileth over all created things! Were the heedless to show forth equity to an extent smaller than a needle's eye, they would behold that they have purposed naught but to compass the good of all; to achieve the welfare of the masses; to purge Thy land of dissension and division; and to adorn it with the evidences of friendliness and concord. For everything there is a sign in Thy realm, and the sign of their sincerity is the manner of their comportment throughout this period, and the patience they have exercised in the midst of hardship. I beseech Thee, O my Begetter, by Thy Name which hath subdued the whole world, and which hath overshadowed all the nations, to lift from their eyes the veil of ignorance, that they may apprehend Thy purpose in sending down Thy laws and ordinances, and revealing Thy commandments in Thy Scriptures and Thy Tablets: for Thou art powerful to do as Thou willest, and supreme over all that Thou desirest. No God is there beside Thee, the Most Exalted, the All-Glorious, the Peerless. O thou who seekest the shadow of the Lote Tree of the Cause, and who dwellest in the meads of bounty and grace! I have recognized the ardour of thy love for God, and the depth of thy devotion to His Countenance. I beseech God, thy Lord, and the Lord of all things, to assist thee at all times; to nourish thee from the stream of bounty and benevolence; and to cause thee to attain unto the highest levels of knowledge and understanding. Consider thou the world, and the evidences of discord rife within it; and reflect upon that which the Tongue of the Will of God hath spoken concerning the desirability of friendliness and unity. The people, truly, have conceived this Mighty Cause and Momentous Enterprise to be a source of mischief and disunity; notwithstanding that the Divine Law commandeth not the creatures but unto affection and the relinquishment of malice. Say: This is a Cause whereby God will make manifest the spiritual characteristics and heavenly acquirements that are latent within man. Therein hath He entertained no other purpose but to induce a progression unto the highest levels of knowledge, and to effect a conquest of the loftiest pinnacle of advancement in the degrees of man. Say: Through it the hyacinths of certitude shall spring up in the earth of the hearts, and the trees of existence shall give forth the blossoms of Divine mysteries and holy utterance in commemoration of the All-Merciful, and in confession of the unity of His Holiness, the All-Glorious. O spiritual friend! Some time hath passed during which, in consequence of a journey, no letter was despatched. The One True God testifieth, and is my witness, that at no time wast thou forgotten; nor, God willing, shalt thou be hereafter. At one of the stages in the journey a letter of thine was perused, and a brief reply was written and sent off. When subsequently admission was gained into the Holy Presence, thy remembrance flowed forth from the Tongue of Grace, and such a demonstration of loving-kindness was witnessed in thy behalf that the pen and the tongue are powerless and inadequate to express or reckon it. Blessed art thou! And again blessed art thou! In truth, the favours of the Ancient King have, in this Most Mighty Revelation, so encompassed His loved ones as to be beyond the ability of anyone, whatever their powers of expression or inquiry, to describe or reckon. It behoveth us to render thanks unto God, the Lord of the realm on high, the King of Glory and Divinity, for as long as the kingdoms of earth and heaven shall endure. Ere this servant had departed on his journey, a Tablet was vouchsafed thee from the Source of loving-kindness; yet in view of certain prudential considerations a delay was incurred in its despatch. Now, in view of the issuance of an unequivocal command, it is enclosed herewith. I beseech God to honour thee with beholding it, even as He had honoured thee with its revelation, in order that the bounty may be perfected, and thine eye may be solaced through the loving-kindness of Him Who is the Lord of the kingdom of bounty and justice. Do thou, on behalf of this servant, convey to the friends of God a matchless and wondrous salutation, and say: "The One True God -- exalted be His glory -- hath in each of the Dispensations of the Manifestations of His own Self reserved trials and tribulations for His loved ones, and destined the detritus of the world for the malevolent and the heedless, appointing afflictions as the test and touchstone of His loved ones, even as He hath said aforetime: 'And We shall try you with somewhat of fear and hunger, and loss of wealth and lives and fruits, etc.' It behoveth you at all times to cling to the cord of steadfastness, and to hold fast the hem of grace. The evanescence of the world, and the ephemerality of all things in it, are matters about which there is no doubt, and no right-minded person will set his heart upon that which must inevitably pass away, nor will he rest satisfied and content with the ease of a few fleeting days. What sapient traveller would be content with the embellishments of the stages in his journey, and forego arrival at his home and destination? Nay, by God! Never will those endued with understanding be debarred by any obstacle, or kept back by even the most refined of this world's perishable benefits from arriving at their ultimate destination and Divine home. We beseech the One True God -- exalted be His glory -- and entertain of Him the hope, that He will at all times dignify His loved ones with the mantle of steadfastness, and, in the midst of suffering, keep them as firm and constant as the immovable mountains. Although, by reason of the succession of afflictions, the body be overcome by sickness, yet shall this pass away, and an everlasting dominion, and a universal and abiding rest and good, ensue. I admonish you, O ye loved ones of God, to guard the pearls of the love of God that ye possess, for thieves lie in wait, and bide their time to divest you of that wherewith ye have been distinguished amongst men. O that the people might know! By God! Were they to apprehend the truth, then would they understand what ye possess, and would offer up their lives in their longing to attain the wonders of the mysteries of knowledge that ye have known, and in their eagerness to acquire the gems of the secrets of certitude which God hath bestowed upon you. Say: 'O Thou Who art the God of all men, and the Lord of the mystery of destiny! We beseech thee by Thy sovereignty which overpowereth the whole world, and by Thy Proof which is manifest among the nations, graciously to aid us to remain steadfast in Thy Cause, through whose appearance the feet of the stalwart have slipped, and the limbs of the resolute have quaked. O Lord! We are weak, and Thou art the Most Powerful, the Almighty. Look not upon us with the eye of justice, but rather with the glances of loving-kindness and grace. Hold then our hands with the hand of Thy bestowal; save us from those floundering in the sloughs of remoteness and deprivation; and deliver us from the guile of those who have strayed far from the shore of the stream of faith. O Thou Who art our God, and the Subjugator of men's necks! Do thou acquaint Thy servants with that which Thou hast distinguished us withal throughout Thy lands, that they may know that we have not purposed to wreak disorder, neither hast Thou commanded us thereunto in Thy Books and Thy Tablets, but rather unto the dissemination of the traces of affection, and the adornment of the world with the robes of friendliness and unity, O Thou Who art the Lord of all men, and the King of the Day of Reckoning!'" We beseech the One True God -- exalted be His grandeur -- to preserve thee at all times, and to enable thee to accomplish that which is purely good. Rest thou assured in the grace of God, and His loving-kindness: He, verily, is with thee, and shall destine for thee all good in His Book. Write thou ever an account of thy circumstances, and despatch it hither; thereto fix thy gaze at all times upon wisdom. He hath said aforetime: "Despair ye not of the mercy of God!" Upon thee be the Glory of God, and His Spirit; and likewise upon those friends of thy Lord, the Most Exalted, the Most Great, who are with thee. Praise be to God, the Lord of the worlds.

From the Most Pure Pen of the Centre of the Covenant, Exalted Be His Praise

He is God

O beloved in the spirit! On this brightsome morn, moved by thy heavenly love, and through the good offices of the attracted leaves, Rúhá Khánum and Khánum Díyá', I have set about writing this luminous leaf, that thou mayest know how dearly thou art cherished -- nor think that thou hast been forgotten -- in these sacred precincts; and that thou mayest not remain quiescent, but constantly tell forth the glad tidings, and be ever filled with fervour, and clamorous with expressions of joy. Upon thee be the Glory of God. Do thou convey my most wondrous Abhá greeting unto thine esteemed spouse, and the rest of thy dependents, male and female alike. 'Ayn 'Ayn

He is God

O beloved one! Do thou convey the expressions of my utmost love and kindness unto thy sister's children, to the degree that it may attract the hearts; and thereto strive that the light of faith may shine forth in their hearts. It is a pity that amongst thy kindred they should remain uninformed, and deprived of the grace of the All-Merciful. Care, association, kindness and love are all incumbent. 'Ayn 'Ayn

He is God

O ye survivors of two holy and blessed souls! Your letter was received. Its contents made clear and evident that through the protection and help of the Ancient Beauty ye remain, after the passing of his honour Sádiq, the august martyr's scion, firm and steadfast in the Cause of God. Ye are related to that servant of the Perspicuous Light, his honour Mishkín. That illustrious soul spent his whole life in humble, self-effacing, loving and sincere devotion to the Cause of God. He was the incarnation of spirit and the embodiment of light; and in outward perfections was distinguished from all his contemporaries. When he perfumed his nostrils with the sweet fragrance of the All-Merciful, he became completely selfless and detached from all else but the True One, sacrificing his own rest and comfort in the path of God. He migrated from Írán to the territory of the Ottomans, and, having dwelt for a while in 'Iráq, hastened to Rumelia. From thence he travelled to the Great City of Istanbul, where he occupied himself with service. He became famed throughout all parts, and was bound in fetters for his love of God. Being subsequently banished from the Great City, he attained in Gallipoli the sacred presence of Bahá'u'lláh, and, accompanying Him on His journey thence, passed his time on board ship with the utmost joy and gladness. Upon our arrival in 'Akká, he was borne off to Cyprus, and confined in the citadel of Famagusta, where, under conditions of the utmost difficulty and hardship, he remained long captive. When the island came into the possession of the English government he was set free. At once he hastened to the Most Great Prison, and joined the companions of Bahá'u'lláh. Day and night he was occupied in transcribing and arranging the Sacred Tablets, and in producing calligraphic renderings of the Greatest Name. These pieces spread throughout all parts, so that in Írán and Túrán, Europe and America, Asia and Africa -- there is no city where some example of his penmanship is not to be found. Most of these pieces are of the Greatest Name. One of the Persian ministers in Paris even related the following: "Ere proceeding to Paris I made first a quick visit to Russia. In the city of Moscow, I was in a state of the utmost sorrow, pain and despair, until, upon entering the home of one of my friends, a highly respectable personage, my eye fell upon a tableau suspended in the upper part of the room, which had been executed with the utmost skill by his honour Mishkín. All at once I was overcome by a feeling of immense joy and happiness. To this day the memory of that joy and happiness abideth with me; nor shall I ever forget it." The person who related this was the minister Mu'ayyiru'l-Mamálik, the son-in-law of Násiri'd-Dín Sháh. He attained the blessing of belief and certitude, and whilst in Paris was occupied with various services. Ye are likewise related to that brilliant candle, his honour Sádiq. That blessed soul beheld his illustrious father, his honour the Beloved of Martyrs, a sacrificial victim on the altar of love. It is evident, therefore, what injuries he sustained. Yet he remained under all circumstances patient, and in all trials constant, until he took his flight unto the Abhá Kingdom, the infinite world. Ye are the relations of these two blessed and holy souls, and very dear in the sight of 'Abdu'l-Bahá. I therefore supplicate at the Blessed Threshold that, under the shadow of God's care and protection, ye may be shielded and preserved from all visitations and afflictions, and that ye may keep the shining lamp of those two illustrious souls ever luminous and refulgent. Do ye follow their example. Firdawsí in the Sháh-Námih saith of Kay-Khusraw:

This happy one doth of two kings signs bewray: * Of Afrásíyáb, likewise of Kávús-Kay

Upon you be the Glory of the Most Glorious. 'Ayn 'Ayn

*The Maidservant of God, Daughter of the martyr, the honoured Leaf Rúhá -- Húríyyih -- Farangís -- Aqdas -- 'Adhrá' -- Husayn Áqá -- Hasan Áqá*

He is God

O ye fruits of the tree of Supreme Sacrifice! That embodiment of spirit hastened unto the field of martyrdom, and that incarnation of light shone forth above the horizon of redemption. He cast upon that family such a ray as shall remain for ever shining and refulgent. Ye are the leaves of that tree and the fruits of that heavenly sadratu'l-muntahá. Do ye appreciate the value of this bounty, and recognize the sublimity of this honour. Strive ye to show forth the utmost freshness, delicacy and sweetness. Upon you by the Glory of the Most Glorious. 'Ayn 'Ayn

*Isfahán. The attracted Maidservant of God Rúhá, Daughter of the late Hájj Mírzá Muhammad-Sádiq, upon him by the Glory of God, the Most Glorious*

He is God

... O grandchild of the martyr in the path of God! The love which 'Abdu'l-Bahá beareth for the survivors of the martyrs is to the degree that the Concourse on high applaud it! These blessed souls laid down their lives. To use the popular expression, "It is no laughing matter." They tasted the venom of the sword, and made their mirror-like breasts the targets of a hundred thousand arrows. How easy it is to say! Now consider them, and consider those others who will not forego one iota of their lusts and passions. Slaves are they of their carnal appetites, and addicted to the pleasures and diversions of this dark and narrow world. Wherefore is there an immeasurable difference betwixt the twain. 'Abdu'l-Bahá cherisheth the wish of perfuming his nostrils with the fragrant dust of these luminous graves. This is my highest hope and my utmost aspiration. I beseech God to grant me this honour, and to enable me to follow their example. May my life be a sacrifice for them. May my heart be a sacrifice for them. I hope that, through the aid and preservation of the Lord of creation, thou wilt be shielded and preserved, and strengthened in thy services to His Holiness the Incomparable; and become a source of glory to the Cause of God. Do thou convey on my behalf kind remembrances and a fragrant greeting unto his honour Áqá Mírzá Husayn Áqá and Hasan Áqá, and unto his honour Mírzá Nusratu'lláh. A letter was written for the believing maidservant of God, Ághá Bíbí, which is enclosed. Do thou deliver it. Upon thee be the Glory of the Most Glorious. 'Abdu'l-Bahá 'Abbás, 21 Rabí'u'l-Avval 1340

He is the Most Glorious

*Sád. The Relatives of their honours the King of Martyrs and the Beloved of Martyrs, upon whom be the Glory of God, the Most Glorious*

He is the Most Glorious

O ye offshoots of the tree of Supreme Sacrifice! Notwithstanding that in these days a fresh affliction hath appeared, and a grievous calamity hath befallen -- the bird of holiness hath wearied of its abode in a strange land, and winged its flight unto its retreat in the Abhá Kingdom -- yet in these days, after the ascension of the Ancient Beauty, life is as death, and death is as life. Upon decease, every confident and steadfast believer, having been released from exile, will settle in his true home; and, having been delivered from estrangement, will join the circle of those who have been admitted into the Court of Grandeur. The atom will revert unto the Sun, and the dewdrop will draw sustenance from the Living Ocean. The thirsty one will find the fountain of life, and the sick one will enter the infirmary of the All-Knowing Physician. In fine, death for the deceased is the mightiest bestowal and the greatest mercy; whereas for the survivors it is the fire of grief and the anguish of separation. Since, however, this separation and deprivation are but for a season, while hereafter we shall all be brought together in the assembly of the world above, and in the Celestial Concourse in the Abhá Kingdom -- whereupon the consuming fire of this separation shall be forgot -- ye should take comfort, and, with patience and fortitude, be occupied with the reviving breezes of the meads of the Covenant, so that at each moment ye may find a fresh spirit and discover a new soul. The Glory of God be upon you. 'Ayn 'Ayn

A Blessed Tablet in honour of Fátimih Begum, the only daughter of the Beloved of Martyrs, who passed away in her youth.

He is God

*The Land of Sád. The Maidservant of God, the illumined Leaf Fátimih Begum, upon her be the Glory of the Most Glorious*

He is God

O thou remnant of the martyrs! Grieve not: the compassionate Beloved is the Assuager of all griefs; that is, His Holiness Bahá'u'lláh. Sorrow not: thy heart and soul shall erelong be gladdened. Weep not; neither do thou lament: recite the Verse of the Most Great Glad Tidings, that thou mayest behold the joy of the world of Divine Unity, and perceive the bounty of the Majestic Lord. The ray of Divine favour hath so shone upon that house and family that its effulgence flasheth in the rising of the horizons of the dawn; while in the morning the gleaming trace of thine august sire extolleth the glory, the unity, the sanctity and the greatness of Him Who was the Author of this most great bounty. Take then a share from the ocean of his happiness, and obtain a portion from the bounty of his servitude. Why, despite such bounties, outpourings and bestowals, wouldst thou weep, wherefore lament? Yea, 'tis cause for untold joy and boundless happiness. 'Ayn 'Ayn

*Isfahán. The Maidservant of God, Fátimih Begum, Daughter of the martyr*

He is the Most Glorious

O thou survivor and memorial of that martyr beloved of the Lord of Grandeur! Whatsoever thou wishest, and whatsoever thou request or say -- all are acceptable in the Court of God. This servant accounteth the good pleasure of that family a means of attainment unto the good pleasure of the True One; for the Blessed Beauty held you in the kindliest regard. Therefore, whatsoever thy straitened heart wisheth, speak forth! Since, however, this matter is connected with the Law of God, this servant cannot breathe a word. For according to the binding injunction of the Book, ere entering upon one's fifteenth year marriage is not permitted. Nomination and betrothal too should not take place before the wedding: that is, after the engagement no more than 95 days should pass before the marriage. Likewise the consent of both parties is the first condition; yet consent before maturity is invalid, while the age of maturity is set at fifteen. Wherefore this servant cannot say aught, for it would contravene the express prescription of the Law of God. Otherwise, by the righteousness of God, I would not spare even mine own life. 'Ayn 'Ayn

A Blessed Tablet beseeching forgiveness for Áqá Mírzá Muhammad-'Alí, scion of his honour the Beloved of Martyrs, upon whom be the Glory of the Most Glorious

He is God

O God, my God! I, verily, make plaint of my grief and sorrow by reason of the sorrows that have assailed me! Hast thou not heard the voice of the mourner, mourning thy distinguished servant, the scion of that august and majestic champion who, with beaming countenance, enkindled heart, and a spirit joyful at its impending ascent unto the kingdom of Thy sanctity, was martyred in Thy path, and his pure blood spilt upon the dust in Thy love? O my Lord! This scion, truly, followed the example of his august father in treading the Straight Path and the Undeviating Way; and passed his days with his eye gladdened by beholding Thy signs, his breast dilated through the breaths of Thy holiness, his tongue eloquent in commemoration of Thee, and his heart staunch in Thy love. O my Lord! He was touched by trials and tribulations, and bore every hardship and adversity, thanking Thee the while for each direst calamity, and each gravest affliction. O my Lord! Never throughout his life did he repose, nor spare any effort in serving Thy loved ones; until he heard the call from the Concourse on high: "O thou tranquil soul! Repair unto thy Lord, pleased and pleasing unto Him." Whereupon he responded to the call; departed this earthly home, and winged his flight unto the kingdom of eternity, the Divine home. O my Lord! Honour his last resting-place, and grant him an exalted seat of truth, transported by the wine of reunion in the Most Sublime Paradise, immersed in the oceans of lights in the Kingdom of Mysteries. Thou, verily, art the All-Pardoner, the Most Precious, the Ever-Forgiving. 'Abdu'l-Bahá 'Abbás, 22 Jím 2 year 1327

He is God

*Sád. The sanctified Leaf, the Maidservant of God Fátimih Begum, Sister of his honour Mírzá Sádiq, upon her be the Glory of God, the Most Glorious*

He is the Most Glorious

O thou holy and luminous leaf! Truly, in the path of God thou wast at all times the dawning-place of calamities and the focus of afflictions. Thou didst drink no draught of water in tranquillity, nor live a day without uttering a heart-consuming sigh. No night didst thou rest on the bed of comfort, nor for a moment didst thou taste the honey of tranquillity of heart and peacefulness of soul. Yet be not saddened, neither be thou sick at heart: for if placidity of heart, tranquillity of spirit, and bodily repose were truly important, praiseworthy and desirable, His Holiness the Prince of Martyrs would assuredly have sought and yearned after them; while all the Prophets and holy ones would have chosen them for themselves. Know therefore that calamities suffered in the path of the True One are bounties; and contentment under His decree is among the characteristics of the people of God. Do thou show the greatest consideration to the spouse of him that hath ascended unto God, and accord her greater honour than before. Likewise do thou educate the children with perfect joy and radiance. 'Ayn 'Ayn

From the Most Pure Pen of His Holiness, The Beloved Guardian of the Cause of God

O thou who hast plucked a brand from the fire of the love of God! Although outwardly communication and correspondence were for a while severed, yet the mystical ties and spiritual communications are at every moment present and unimpaired. That tireless servant of the Sacred Threshold is accounted among the well-favoured believers, and numbered with the steadfast and faithful maidservants of the Abhá Beauty. Thou shalt not pass from memory, nor in these sacred precincts be forgot. Wherefore with a gladsome heart and a tranquil spirit do thou pursue the path of service. He will assist thee, and grant thee victory and triumph. The servant of His Threshold, Shoghi

*For the attention of the Maidservant of God Rúhá Khánum-i-Maghzí, upon her be the Glory of God*

Honoured lady, thy letter arrived in the most luminous court, and was graced by the most holy glances of the beloved of mankind, his Holiness the Guardian of the Cause of God -- may my soul be a sacrifice for his favours. The contents of the letter gave evidence of the Divine bounties and heavenly confirmations which -- praise be to God -- have surrounded thee on every hand. Whereof indeed there could be no greater, higher, more perfect or more glorious a proof than thy success in forming an assembly wherein thou hast brought together, in a forum of spiritual fellowship, a group of steadfast, well-grounded, enkindled maidservants of the All-Merciful, to whom thou art providing lessons in teaching the Cause. This outstanding service is in itself an incomparable bounty wherewith thou hast been blessed, honoured and distinguished. As the recipient, therefore, of so bountiful a favour, thou hast reason for the utmost happiness, joy and radiance. Do thou most certainly continue thine endeavours, and provide the means for perfecting and arranging this luminous gathering as is most requisite and fitting, so that it may become in all respects beloved, agreeable, acceptable and satisfactory. The pains and efforts of that honoured maidservant in this regard are undoubtedly favoured with approval and acceptance in the Court of the All-Knowing King. To all the maidservants of the Merciful who are members of the blessed assembly -- Sughrá Begum Núrí-Zádih, Bíbí Mishkín Fakhru'l-Mulúk-i-Mahbúbíyyih, Ruqíyyih Khánum-i-Bádkúbi'í, Mulkí-Ján-i-Ábádi'í, 'Adhrá' Khánum-i-Mahbúbíyyih, Munavvar Khánum, Ridváníyyih Khánum, Ádharmídukht-i-Maghzí, upon them be the Glory of God, the Most Glorious -- we express the most cordial felicitations; and our wish and hope at the Sacred Threshold on behalf of each one of them is for a yet greater measure of success and spiritual advancement. Know thou of a certainty that they are under the shadow of the glances of God's loving providence, and watched over by the eyes of the gracious favours of His Holiness the All-Merciful. Written by his blessed order. Núri'd-Dín Zayn, Rajab 1347, 21 December 1928

Section Seven

The Martyrdom of

His Honour Mullá Kázim-i-Tálkhúnchi'í

And the Apprehension of

His Honour Áqá Siyyid Áqá Ján, Upon Him Be the Glory of God

**
**

*Account of the Martyrdom of His Honour Mullá Kázim-i-Tálkhúnchi'í*

The village of Tálkhúnchih is one of the settlements in the environs of Isfahán. In those days no more than a handful of the friends of God resided there. One day, Mullá Kázim and Áqá Siyyid Áqá Ján, who were both servants of the Threshold of the Blessed Beauty, attended a gathering, which included also a number of Muslims. Mullá Kázim was engaged in smoking a narghile when all at once, without warning and for no apparent cause, one of the company, a religious bigot, raised the cry: "Ho, for shame! The pipe hath been defiled! This man is a Bahá'í!" Others too, emulating this ignorant man, raised a similar outcry. Siyyid Áqá Ján would fain have extinguished with the water of admonition and counsel the fire kindled in these rude souls; but they paid no heed to the admonitions of the loving counsellor, and, hurling themselves upon the two unfortunates, fiercely assailed them with wounding blows and insults. Not content with this, they then wrote an account of the incident to Shaykh Báqir the "Wolf," who in turn sent a message to Zillu's-Sultán instructing him to send several officials to bring the accused to Isfahán. The governor acted as bidden by the benighted cleric, and a band of ruffians proceeded to Tálkhúnchih; brought those two intimates of the Divine Court, with bared head and bare feet, on foot to Isfahán; and bore them into the presence of Shaykh Báqir. When the Shaykh's gaze fell upon the hapless pair he ordered them, after a deal of recrimination and expressions of ill-humour, to show through abuse and execration that they had renounced their faith, threatening them at the same time with death. But those two adorers of the True Beloved voiced abhorrence at the idea, exclaiming, "Would to God that we had one hundred thousand lives to lay down in His path!" At this, the flame of Shaykh Báqir's anger blazed up, and he sent word to Zillu's-Sultán to crucify them, and to adorn the gallows with their bodies. Zillu's-Sultán was at first hesitant to take their lives; but fearing as a result of Shaykh Báqir's reiterated threats for his leadership and position, he at length decided to put one of them to death. To this end he resolved that Mullá Kázim should die; while Siyyid Áqá Ján he excused from the sentence of death on account of his holy lineage. The Shaykh gave to outward seeming his consent to this proposal, and requested the governor to order his executioner to carry out the sentence. He then sent a crier abroad into the city to make a public proclamation; and, to the sound of drum and trumpet, he bore the wronged pair into the Maydán. That day was the twentieth of the month of Safar 1296 A.H. One of the followers of the Shaykh ventured to observe: "Today is the fortieth day after the martyrdom of the Prince of Martyrs, and shouldst thou defer this person's execution until the following day it would be preferable." The Shaykh replied however: "Precisely because it is the fortieth, the recompense merited by the action will be all the greater;" and delivered Mullá Kázim to the executioner. The latter at first ordered him to announce his repentance, and renunciation of the Cause; but his words had no effect, since Mullá Kázim remained as firm and steadfast as before in his love for the Abhá Beloved. Finally, the executioner severed the head of that great-souled hero from his body; and, that his victim might suffer the greater agony, so wielded his sword that it only slowly and gradually performed its task. Thereafter, at the Shaykh's bidding, the victim's body was suspended from the gallows. While this was in progress, however, the cord snapped. Pursuant to the Shaykh's orders, he was once more suspended from the gallows, but this time in such a manner that his neck and breast were hanging downwards, and his feet were raised aloft. The Shaykh announced: "Whoever casteth a stone at the one here suspended shall earn a mighty recompense." It is related that there was a lady who had been seized by the pangs of childbirth, yet still, in such a state, rose up and proceeded to the Maydán in order to cast a stone at that wronged one. Nor, whatever remonstrations were addressed to her, such as, "Thou art in labour, and like to bring upon thyself grievous hurt and calamity," would she be admonished, but went regardless to cast her stone at the martyr. That day, the children who chanced to meet each other boasted: "My mother went to cast a stone."

That pure body was still suspended at eventide when a group of people arrived and, kindling a fire, burnt his beard; cut off his lips, ears and nose; and gouged out his eyes from their sockets. Later too, at the Shaykh's behest, another company arrived and stoned him. Likewise on the second night others came and sundered him limb from limb. On the third day, the Shaykh came into the Maydán, and beheld that pure body thus dismembered and caked in dust and blood. Pursuant to the orders which he then immediately issued, a group of horsemen mounted their steeds, and galloped them over the noble temple of the martyr, pounding his sacred body beneath their horses' hooves. This done, they flung his remains into a well. As for Siyyid Áqá Ján, by Shaykh Báqir's order he was on the same day of his arrest bastinadoed and soundly beaten. Thereafter, again by the latter's order, his ears were cut off, and a halter was placed around his neck wherewith he was paraded about the city's thoroughfares and markets. Finally, he was cast into prison, where he tarried for a month. On the day when, at their behest, the Twin Shining Lights were martyred, the Shaykh and the Imám wished to have Siyyid Áqá Ján slain too. Learning, however, of this intention, Zillu's-Sultán summoned the latter before him; and, since he had from the outset vouchsafed him an assurance of safety, ordered that he should not bide in Isfahán, but leave the city. Accompanied by officials, Siyyid Áqá Ján accordingly departed from Isfahán. On his way he had the happy fortune to encounter their honours Nabíl-i-Qá'iní and Amín, to whom he recounted what had befallen him. Nabíl and Amín then set off for Qazvín, and related details of the story to the friends. After so much pain and hardship, Siyyid Áqá Ján became the object of God's loving favour; and in a Tablet Bahá'u'lláh indicates that although he was not martyred, he still has an estimable station in the eyes of God.

His honour Mírzá Ashraf-i-Ábádi'í, another of the martyrs of the Land of Sád, was slain at the behest of the son of the Wolf. His Holiness the Guardian of the Cause of God -- exalted be his praise -- provides in the blessed tablet *God Passes By* a description of this event, whose purport in Persian is as follows:

In Isfahán Mírzá Ashraf was martyred, and his body trampled underfoot. This deed was the work of Shaykh Muhammad-Taqí, the son of the Wolf. His body was finally surrendered to the people, who, having fed with it the flames of a fire, deposited what remained of it in a place over which they destroyed a wall. *Finis*.

His honour Hájí Mírzá Haydar-'Alíy-i-Isfahání relates the following: "... The family of Áqá Mírzá Ashraf came originally from Bushrúyih. A Siyyid, he was born in Najaf-Ábád and educated in Isfahán. He was a divine and a scholar, and extremely sincere and devoted to the Cause. The Bahá'ís of Ábádih took him to Ábádih, where they provided him with a home and furnishings. Here he remained for well nigh thirty years, even becoming known as Mírzá Ashraf-i-Ábádi'í." *Finis*. The martyrdom of Mírzá Ashraf took place around the year 1307 A.H.

Others too hastened into the arena of martyrdom in Isfahán, both during the ministry of the Exalted Lord, and during those of the Ancient Beauty and the Centre of the Covenant. Ustád Muhammad-'Alíy-i-Salmání, who passed away in 'Ishqábád in 1324 A.H., records in his autobiography, which he wrote with his own pen, the names of a number of Bábís he himself had seen, who in some cases had been slaughtered, and in others apprehended and their ears nailed to a post ..." For information concerning the rest of the martyrs, reference may be had to the history of the Blessed Cause, and to the Tablets revealed in this regard. By way of example, I provide at this point an extract from the reminiscences of Lieutenant Ridá-Qulíy-i-Níkú-Bín concerning a number of the friends who suffered martyrdom and persecution.

At that period, when the soul-stirring call of the beloved Cause had produced a profound effect in all horizons and souls -- when in every town there was a stir and in every land a tumult -- the Muslims, acting at the prompting of their clergy, omitted no form of iniquity or oppression in their dealings with the generality of the Bahá'ís. *To cite an instance of this treatment:* In 1321 A.H. there occurred the disturbance named after the Russian consulate, a highly significant event which was of so grave a character that its flame overspread the face of Írán; but as a result of which the name of the Cause resonated more powerfully, and the cries of its impassioned lovers reached the ears of a greater number of those previously uninformed of it than ever before. Were I to relate the preliminaries of this disturbance, and to dwell upon the woes and vicissitudes the beloved friends suffered throughout its course, the account would become wearisome, and deflect me from my purpose. This much may be briefly stated that, in consequence of the successive afflictions and trials which they had long borne at the hands of the Muslims, the Bahá'ís had reached the point of desperation; and, on the advice of a number of leading figures of the age, including his honour Mírzá Hasan-i-Adíb (who had at that time newly arrived from Tihrán *en route* to Shíráz); Mírzá Asadu'lláh Khán-i-Vazír; Mírzá Muhammad Khán-i-Lashkar-Nivís, Mírzá Ahmad Khán-i-Fátihu'l-Mulk, Hájí Mírzá Muhammad-Sádiq, son of the Beloved of Martyrs, and one or two officers of the Fawj-i-Jalálí, all, men and women alike, took refuge in the Russian consulate, seeking a decisive clarification of their status which, they hoped, might convey also an assurance of their freedom. Since the Consul was not himself present in Isfahán, his deputy submitted the matter -- both the representation of grievances and the appeal for justice -- to the royal court of Muzaffari'd-Dín Sháh, strongly urging that one of the two following courses be adopted: either that the Bahá'ís should be completely free, or that some other status should be determined for them. In order to achieve their object, the friends remained for more than twelve days in the aforesaid premises; yet for those few days, with what ineffable spirituality did the cry "Yá Bahá'u'l-Abhá!" fill the air of the place! How thrillingly did the soul-quickening recitations of Tablets and prayers cause the hearts to quiver! And how captivatingly did the children, though only of tender years, occupy themselves both day and night with singing heart-reviving melodies! For their maintenance, his excellency the Minister and his honour the Accountant (Lashkar-Nivís), girding up the loins of their endeavour, spared no expense in procuring necessary provisions. At length an undertaking was obtained from the Muslims to guarantee the safety of the Bahá'ís, which took the form of an oath, sworn on the glorious Qur'án, that they would no longer inflict harm on that community, but leave them to live their lives in peace. Once a modicum of assurance had been gained on this score, the Bahá'ís resolved to leave the consulate and to go about their normal business. No sooner had they emerged from the premises, however, than they were set upon by a mean rabble of the populace, and became embroiled in a violent fracas and upheaval. In the resulting turmoil, one Siyyid Abu'l-Qásim of Márnán near Isfahán was martyred, and his body lost without trace. Two other souls, Hájí Husayn and Hájí Hádí, both merchants of Isfahán, were martyred in the Maydán-i-Sháh, and their bodies set alight with oil. The remainder of the friends, having contrived by whatever exertions to deliver themselves from beneath the hands and feet of their assailants, in some cases made their way home, and in others quit the city. The effects of this general commotion and upheaval at once communicated themselves to the other cities of Írán, particularly to Yazd and some other parts, where an extraordinary tumult was engendered. *To cite another example:* On the night of a celebration and firework display which Zillu's-Sultán had arranged in the Bágh-i-Káj, and to which he had brought along also several members of our regimental band, he announced in a loud voice, which all present heard: "Know ye what night is this? It is the night whereon the God of the Bábís died!" Hearing this pronouncement on such a night -- coming as it did from the mouth of the outstanding personage in Írán at that epoch -- I fell to thinking, and in bemused wonderment asked myself: "What god is this who has died?" In fine, I was for long submerged in an ocean of bewilderment. *To cite yet another example:* There was in Isfahán a certain Mullá Sálih, who was a native of Tálkhúnchih, one of the dependencies of the city. He had a very famous and well-known school, which was patronized for the most part by nobles and dignitaries. He had too a general acquaintance with my father, and the latter accordingly entrusted my education to him. Hence, when my military exercises were complete, I would spend the rest of my time learning my lessons and applying myself to calligraphic exercises. So matters continued for a space. When the time arrived for the regiment to be dismissed, I repaired as usual to the country, and returned a while later to the city. One morning, as I was crossing the Maydán-i-Sháh on my way to the parade ground, I observed that a large crowd were forcibly dragging a poor wretch, whom they held captive in their midst, in the direction of the Masjid-i-Sháh, beating him the while with sticks, and belabouring him with blows and curses. Upon my approaching to inquire who it was, I was informed: "It is a Bábí: they want to take him to Áqá Najafí and obtain from him a death warrant so as to have him slain." Much affected by the spectacle, I drew closer, and all at once beheld that the subject of these proceedings was none other but the aforesaid Mullá Sálih. Despite myself, I exclaimed: "Áqá Mírzá, is it indeed thou?!" ("Áqá Mírzá" was in those days the appellation used for teachers.) Observing this reaction, the people glared at me as though they had a mind to inflict the like treatment upon me too; in view, however, of my military attire they had not courage to do so, but, turning their attention again to Mullá Sálih, continued beating the unfortunate man. He in the meantime fastened upon me imploring glances that seemed to bespeak an appeal for succour and redress; but of course what could one helpless child accomplish in the face of a hostile and powerful multitude? In view of the cordial attachment and deep-seated affection which I entertained for my teacher, my feelings all at once overcame me, and I involuntarily fell to weeping. Starting to cry aloud, I turned towards the crowd; but as it chanced, at that same moment an officer, a native of Tálkhúnchih who was acquainted with my father, appeared upon the scene. Running at once towards him, I pleaded: "This person is our teacher: don't let them beat him! They want to kill him!" The officer replied: "Knowest thou not forsooth that this is a Bábí? Let them beat him! Should they wish to kill him, what is it to thee that he was once thy teacher? Go and attend to thine own affairs!" Seeing, however, that his admonitions produced no effect on me, he carried me off from thence; and, once away from the crowd, I betook me to my father, and explained to him exactly what had taken place. No sooner was my father informed how matters stood than he exclaimed indignantly: "So then, Sergeant 'Alí (the name of the aforesaid officer) hath revealed his malice against poor Mullá Sálih!" With this, he arose from his place, and left the room to see about effecting the Mullá's deliverance. An hour later he brought back the Mullá, bare-headed and bare-footed as before, and that night conveyed him surreptitiously out of the city. In fine, after a certain period, when the business had lost its novelty, the Mullá came again into the city, and resumed his former occupation.

* * *

Section Eight

The Fate of Those Who Caused

The Martyrdom of

The Twin Shining Lights

It was not long after the passing of the Twin Shining Lights that the implacable persecutors and instigators of the martyrdom of those two wronged ones were each afflicted with the most grievous torment, and overtaken by the avenging wrath of God. One was banished and expelled from Isfahán, ending his days in the utmost humiliation and abasement, while the other was visited with a fatal wound and virulent sickness which caused all his relatives, his wife and children, to shrink from him in disgust and loathing. Zillu's-Sultán incurred the ire of Násiri'd-Dín Sháh; the extent of his government, which had included most of the territories of Írán, was restricted to Isfahán; and eventually he left Írán for foreign parts, remaining long bewildered and unsettled. Returning later to Írán, he was afflicted with a condition of acute insanity, which robbed him entirely of the use of his wits and reason, to the degree that he even consumed his own bodily excretions; and finally, in the utmost wretchedness, he yielded up his life. His body was transported to Mashhad in Khurásán, where it was laid to rest. On the way thither a hungry dog managed to intrude itself into his coffin by night, and ate a quantity of his flesh and bone, thereby fulfilling the purport of a blessed utterance of 'Abdu'l-Bahá in his respect: "O God! Do Thou set over him a dog, that it may gnaw all his bones!" Contemporary historians such as Muhammad-Hasan Khán, Saní'u'd-Dawlih (the son of Hájí 'Alí Khán, Hájibu'd-Dawliy-i-Marághi'í) and others have in their works paid various tributes to him, and made him the object of their praise. For example, in the fifth volume of his *Mir'átu'l-Buldán-i-Násirí*, Saní'u'd-Dawlih has drawn the likeness of Zillu's-Sultán, and described the grandeur of his station; and even though Zillu's-Sultán had a squint, and looked askance, he has represented him in the depiction as whole and sound, nor at all stinted himself in servile blandishments. In the Holy Tablets he has been referred to as the "Fading Shadow." In this connection, I shall cite here what I have written in the second volume of the work *Rahíq-i-Makhtúm*.

"Fading Shadow"

Intended by the expression is Prince Mas'úd Mírzá, Zillu's-Sultán, the son of Násiri'd-Dín Sháh, who occasioned in Isfahán the martyrdoms of the Twin Shining Lights; of Mírzá Ashraf-i-Najaf-Ábádí, resident in Ábádih; and of Mullá Kázim-i-Tálkhúnchi'í; and who strenuously opposed the Blessed Cause. In a Tablet to Mír Muhammad-Husayn Big-i-Bushrúyi'í, the Blessed Beauty explains the reason for his opposition to the Faith of God as follows.

*His exalted Utterance:*

It is a matter of astonishment that until now the Sháh of Persia hath not adverted to the loving-kindness, the patience and the clemency extended to him from on high. Do thou beseech the One True God to make the Sháh aware. His real enemy is his son, Zillu's-Sultán. All know that he despatched Sayyáh unto the Most Great Prison especially to set afoot a great sedition; the which being denied him, he rose up in opposition to the Cause. The Sháh too credited his fantasies and fabrications, and surrendered the cities and regions of God unto the most ravening wolf on the surface of the earth. In the whole world there hath not been, nor is there, his like or equal for villainy and malice. Some while previously We spake this most exalted Word: "Of the blood of God's loved ones he, verily, hath quaffed what neither the Tigris, nor the Euphrates, nor the Jayhún, nor the Sayhún, can equal ..."

(Date of the Tablet: 9 Jím 1, year 1309 A.H.)

His Holiness the Guardian of the Cause of God writes in the Centennial Tablet to the American friends words to this effect:

"...The tyrannical and cruel prince Mas'úd Mírzá, Zillu's-Sultán, the eldest son of Násiri'd-Dín Sháh, who held sway over two fifths of his father's dominions, and was stigmatised by the pen of His Holiness Bahá'u'lláh as the "Infernal Tree," was in the end overtaken by ill-fortune and disaster. The extent of his dominions was limited to Isfahán, and he was stripped and deprived of all his former respect, honour, rank and glory. Jalálu'd-Dawlih, who was branded by the Supreme Pen as "The Oppressor of the Land of Yá'," was, a year after the bloodshed and mischief he had committed, deposed and summoned to Tihrán, where he was forced to return a part of the property he had stolen from his oppressed victims. (The Centennial Tablet of America, p. 232)

A portion of the blessed utterances of 'Abdu'l-Bahá touching Zillu's-Sultán will be presented at this juncture.

*His most sweet utterance:*

"... In Switzerland, we were making our way towards the hotel, which was built atop a mountain, when all at once I noticed that a strange figure wearing a Western-style hat had fallen in with our company, and was walking close beside me. When I looked at him, he came forward, made obeisance, and said: "Pray sir, art thou not 'Abbás Effendi?" "I cannot deny it!" I replied. "I have been greatly desirous of meeting thee," he continued, "I shall come again. Be sure that I shall come again." With this, he took his leave of me and went his way. Thereafter we met on numerous occasions. In Paris, he stayed at a hotel at a cost of fifteen French guineas a day. The hotel staff also received from him fifteen guineas. To bid him welcome, they called him "Prince," which gratified him. He invited us to a meal in that hotel, and put on a very splendid affair -- it was a regular banquet. He sought repeatedly to distance himself from the death of the King of Martyrs, and to represent himself as blameless in the matter. When a suitable moment presented itself, I said: "Very good, thou wast not responsible for the death of the martyrs: would it not have been well to restore their property?" -- to which he gave absolutely no reply. His all-consuming wish was that I should reveal to him his future, for he was intent on wielding a controlling influence in Írán. Although he did not use the word "kingship," he wished to be the most influential figure in Írán. Finally one day he put the matter into words, and said: "I wish to hear my future from thy tongue: what doth it hold in store?" I told him: "We are no soothsayer: none but God hath knowledge of the unseen. An intelligent person may, however, make certain deductions. What I know is this, that thou must put all vain imaginings out of thy head. The things thou wishest for shall never be; but I guarantee that thy wealth shall be preserved: safe from any danger, this wealth shall remain for thee and for thine expenses. I told him plainly: "The other things shall never come about, but thy wealth is safe, rest assured thereof." To a degree he *was* assured, although inwardly he still wished for influence and power. One day I went for a walk in the Bois de Boulogne. All at once I saw that Zillu's-Sultán had arrived and was alighting from a carriage. He had also a woman in his company. Then, as he made his way over to me, and fell into conversation, the son of Nizámu'l-'Ulamá'-i-Tabrízí appeared, and likewise made obeisance. Zillu's-Sultán began extolling him, saying, "This gentleman is the son of the Nizámu'l-'Ulamá'. What good friends this family have been to the Qájár family! What services they have rendered! And withal how favourably have they ever been regarded by the Qájárs!" He continued protractedly in this vein until we wearied of it. At length, the son of the Nizámu'l-'Ulamá' took his leave and departed. No sooner had he gone than Zillu's-Sultán exclaimed, "Áqá! Dost thou mark this fellow? -- a rascally knave, whose like the world hath not seen!" and he set to reviling him. He said: "Now will he go and tell his comrades that Zillu's-Sultán was e'en now in the company of the Áqá!" Ismá'íl Mírzá and Akbar Mírzá (the sons of Zillu's-Sultán), and Jalálu'd-Dawlih also came to me. Jalálu'd-Dawlih showed forth great lowliness, and several times came to express repentance for his deeds ..."

(Blessed talk in Haifa, 2 -- year 1916)

Zillu's-Sultán was exceedingly ruthless, and did not shrink from any kind of action or proceeding, no matter how ugly and repellent. It is related that he had two very large and rapacious hounds, which he fed and cared for with his own hand. One day, in search of sport, he took them with him out of the city. On the way, a wretched cultivator presented to him a letter complaining of the injustice and cruelty of the headman of his village. Zillu's-Sultán, who was on horseback, took the letter, and, having glanced at it, made of a sudden a sign to the two rapacious hounds; whereat the bloodthirsty creatures flew with mortal intent upon that poor defenceless cultivator, and tore his body to shreds. The Qájár prince, august scion of the "victorious" monarch Násiri'd-Dín Sháh -- he who is considered the embodiment of "fateful power," of "mighty splendour" and of "heavenly elevation" -- gazed at this fearsome spectacle, and from the very excess of delight and pleasure it afforded him emitted loud guffaws of laughter. By the testimony of history, the world has seen many people of this kind who derived pleasure from the pain and suffering of the victims of oppression.
